§ 53.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BOD (BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND). Shall have the same meaning as defined in
the §
51.25.
   COMMERCIAL STORM WATER SURCHARGE. An additional charge which is billed to
commercial users for treating storm water in excess of normal residential storm
water discharge.
   COUNCIL. The Town Council of Parker City, Indiana, or any duly authorized
officials acting on its behalf.
   DEBT SERVICE COSTS. The average annual principal and interest payments on
all outstanding revenue bonds or other long-term capital debt.
   ERU. Equivalent residential unit. One ERU shall be equivalent to 3,600
square feet of impervious material for each residential user. Unless otherwise
noted, each residential user shall be charged a base rate of one ERU per
residential customer unless otherwise indicated.
   IMPERVIOUS MATERIAL. Material that prohibits the direct passage of
penetration of precipitation directly into the soil or ground and shall include
gravel. Said material shall be human-made and placed so that precipitation
shall be diverted or collected rather than have a direct passage to the ground.
Ponds or retention pools designed for collection of storm water shall not be
included in this definition.
   INDUSTRIAL WASTES. The wastewater discharges from industrial, trade, or
business processes as distinct from employee wastes or wastes from sanitary
conveniences.
   INITIAL CONNECTION PERIOD. Any time after substantial completion of the
storm water system as determined by the agreement between the town and the
contractor constructing the system and the date that the users are notified of
substantial completion.
   NORMAL RESIDENTIAL STORM WATER DISCHARGE. For the purpose of determining
surcharges shall mean storm water that is normal for a residential user or
building.
   NPDES (NATIONAL POLLUTANT DISCHARGE ELIMINATION SYSTEM) PERMIT. Shall have
the same meaning as defined in §
51.25.
   OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE COSTS. Include all costs, direct and indirect,
necessary to provide adequate storm water collection, transportation, and
management on a continuing basis and produce discharges to receiving waters
that conform with all related federal, state, and local requirements. These
costs shall include replacement.
   OTHER SERVICE CHARGES. Tap charges, connection charges, area charges, and
other identifiable charges, other that user charges, debt service charges, and
excessive strength surcharges.
   PERSON. Any and all persons, natural or artificial, including any
individual, firm, company, municipal or private corporation, association,
society, institution, enterprise, governmental agency, or other entity.
   REPLACEMENT COSTS. The expenditures for obtaining and installing equipment,
accessories, or appurtenances which are necessary during the useful life of the
storm water system to maintain the capacity and performance for which such
system was designed and constructed.
   SHALL. The act referred to is mandatory; MAY is permissive.
   STORM WATER. The water which is received by the town and its residents from
precipitation that occurs as a result of climatic changes and storm events.
   STORM WATER SEWAGE SYSTEM. The entire storm water collection and discharge
system for the town as set forth in this chapter.
   STORM WATER USE ORDINANCE. A separate and companion enactment to this
chapter, which regulates the connection to and use of public and private storm
water sewer systems.
   TOWN. The Town of Parker City, Indiana acting by and through the Town
Council.
   USER CLASS. The division of storm water customers by source, function,
characteristics, and process or discharge similarities (i.e., residential,
multi-family residential, mobile home park, commercial, industrial,
institutional, and governmental in user charge system).
      (1)   COMMERCIAL USER. Any establishment involved in a commercial
enterprise, business, or service, based on a determination by the town.
      (2)   GOVERNMENTAL USER. Any federal, state, or local governmental user
of the storm water system.
      (3)   INDUSTRIAL USER. Any manufacturing or processing facility.
      (4)   INSTITUTIONAL USER. Any establishment involved in a social,
charitable, religious, and/or educational function based on a determination by
the town.
      (5)   NON-RESIDENTIAL USER. Any user of a structure that is not a single
family residence. Those users shall include, but are not limited to the
following.
         (a)   MOBILE HOME PARK USER. An area on which at least two mobile
homes, other than mobile homes on permanent foundations, are harbored on
temporary supports for the purpose of being occupied as principal residences.
         (b)   MULTI-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL USER. A user of the storm water system
whose premises or building is used as a multi-family residence.
      (6)   RESIDENTIAL USER. A user of the storm water system whose premises
or building is used primarily as a single-family residence for one or more
persons. Any residence that also conducts a home based business shall be
considered to be a non-residential user and not eligible for the RESIDENTIAL
USER rate.
   WASTEWATER FACILITIES. The structures, equipment, and processes required to
collect, carry away, and treat domestic and commercial wastes and dispose of
the effluent.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.02 USER CLASSES.
   (A)   (1)   Every person whose premises are served by said storm water
system shall be charged for services provided. These charges are established
for each user class, as defined, in order that the storm water system shall
recover, from each user and user class, revenue which is proportional to its
use of the treatment works in terms of volume and load.
      (2)   User charges are levied to defray the cost of operation and
maintenance (including replacement) of the treatment works. User charges shall
be uniform in magnitude within a user class.
   (B)   User charges are subject to the rules and regulations adopted by
federal and state agencies. Replacement costs, which are recovered through the
system of user charges, shall be based upon the expected service life of the
storm water system appurtenances.
   (C)   The various classes of users of the treatment works, for the purposes
of this chapter, shall be as follows:
      (1)   Class 1: Residential;
      (2)   Class 2: Non-residential;
      (3)   Class 2.1: Multi-family residential/mobile home park;
      (4)   Class 2.2: Commercial;
      (5)   Class 2.3: Governmental/institutional;
      (6)   Class 2.4: Industrial; and
      (7)   Class 2.5: All other non-residential users.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.03 RATES AND CHARGES.
   (A)   For the use of and the service rendered by the storm water system,
rates and charges shall be collected from the owners of each and every lot,
parcel of real estate, or building that is connected with the town storm water
system or otherwise discharges liquids, either directly or indirectly, into the
storm water system of the town.
   (B)   Such rates and charges include user charges, debt service costs,
excessive strength surcharges, and other service charges, which rates and
charges shall be payable as herein provided and shall be in an amount
determinable as follows.
      (1)   (a)   The storm water rates and charges shall be based on the
quantity of water discharged on or in the property or premises subject to such
rates and charges as calculated by the town.
         (b)   For the purpose of billing and collecting the charges for storm
water services, the usage schedule on which the amount of said rates and
charges shall be determined, beginning on September 1, 2018 is as follows:
Non-residential users                              Class 2
   Commercial users                             Class 2.2
      Base rate per month
         All users                        $3
   Governmental/institutional users             Class 2.3
      Base rate per month
         All users                        $3
   Industrial users                             Class 2.4
      Base rate per month
         All users                        $3
   Multi-family residential/mobile home park useClass 2.1
      Charge per mobile home                 $3
   All other non-residential users              Class 2.5
      Base rate per month
         All users                        $3
Residential users                                  Class 1
   Base rate: as follows
   Base rate per month                          Charge for each ERU
      All users                              $3
 
      (2)   Inspection and connection fees are as follows: inspection fee shall
be $5 for a final inspection of any and all connections to the storm water
system.
      (3)   For service rendered to the town, said town shall be subject to the
same rates and charges herein above provided.
      (4)   All residential and non-residential users shall be assessed a
minimum monthly base fee of $3. In the event that the actual quantity of the
square footage of impervious material is less than 3,600 square feet, the
minimum rate shall apply.
      (5)   Beginning on January 1, 2019, the rates under divisions (B)(1) to
(B)(4) above shall increase by $0.50.
      (6)   Beginning on January 1, 2020, the rates under divisions (B)(1) to
(B)(4) above shall increase an additional $0.50, so the new rate will be $4.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008; Ord. 2018-7, passed 8-16-2018) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.04 QUANTITY ALLOWANCES.
   (A)   The quantity of storm water discharged into the storm water system and
obtained from sources other than the utility that serves the town shall be
determine by the town in such manner as the town shall reasonably elect, and
the storm water service shall be billed at the above appropriate rates; except
as is hereinafter provided in this section, the town may make proper allowances
in determining the storm water bill for quantities of water shown on the
records to be consumed, but which are also shown to the satisfaction of the
town that such quantities do not actually flow from the property.
   (B)   In the event a lot, parcel of real estate, or building discharges
sanitary sewage, industrial wastes, water, or other liquids into the town storm
water system, either directly or indirectly, or is otherwise not acceptable to
the town storm water system, then the user shall be assessed any and all costs,
fines, penalties, attorney fees, and any other expense associated with the
improper discharge into the storm water system.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.05 RATE ADJUSTMENTS.
   In order that the rates and charges may be justly and equitable adjusted to
the service rendered to users, the town shall base its charges only on the
square feet of impervious area as well as the costs for operation and
maintenance of the storm water system.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.06 BILLING AND COLLECTION PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Such rates and charges shall be prepared, billed, and collected by the
town in the manner provided by law and ordinance.
   (B)   The rates and charges for all users shall be prepared and billed
monthly.
   (C)   The rates and charges for all users shall be billed to and paid by the
owner of the property.
   (D)   As is provided by statute, all rates and charges not paid when due are
declared to be delinquent and a penalty of 10% of the amount of the rates or
charges shall thereupon attach thereto. The time at which such rates shall be
paid is now fixed at 15 days after the date of mailing of the bill.
   (E)   In the event that it is necessary to institute any proceedings to
collect any past due amount, then the owner of the property shall be
responsible for all collection costs, fees, reasonable attorney fees, court
costs, or other expenses incurred by the town.
   (F)   Delinquent storm water fees and penalties shall constitute a lien
against the real property against which the user fees have been imposed. Such
liens shall be certified to the County Auditor and collected as provided in
I.C. 36-9-23-32.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.07 STORM WATER STUDIES.
   (A)   (1)   In order that the rates and charges for storm water services may
be in proportion to the cost of providing services to the various users or user
classes, the town may cause a study to be made from time to time.
      (2)   Such study may include, but not be limited to, an analysis of the
costs associated with the collecting, controlling, and discharging of the storm
water volume and delivery flow rate characteristics attributed to the various
users or user classes, the financial position of the storm water utility and
the adequacy of its revenue to provide reasonable funds for the operation and
maintenance, replacements, debt service requirements and capital improvements
to the storm water systems.
      (3)   The town may adjust its rates and charges to reflect the results of
the study.
   (B)   (1)   Said studies shall be conducted by officers or employees of the
town, or by a firm of certified public accountants or a firm of consulting
engineers which firms shall have experience in such studies, or by such
combination of officers, employees, certified public accountants, or engineers
as the town shall determine to be best under the circumstances.
      (2)   The town may, upon completion of said study, revise and adjust
rates and charges, as necessary in accordance therewith in order to maintain
the proportionality and sufficiency of the rates.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.08 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The town shall make and enforce such laws and regulations as may be
deemed necessary for the safe, economical, and efficient management of the
town’s storm water system and storm water conveyance system, for the
construction and use of storm water and for the regulation, collection,
rebating, and refunding of such rates and charges.
   (B)   The town is authorized to prohibit dumping of wastes into the town’s
storm water system which, in its discretion, are deemed harmful to the
operation of the storm water system works of the town.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.09 SPECIAL RATE CONTRACTS.
   The Council is further authorized to enter into special rate contracts with
customers of the storm water system where clearly definable cost to the storm
water system can be determined, and such rate shall be limited to such costs.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.10 APPEAL PROCEDURE.
   The rules and regulations promulgated by the town, after approval of the
Town Council shall, among other things, provide for an appeal procedure whereby
a user shall have the right to appeal a decision concerning user charges of the
Town Council and may be appealed to a court of competent jurisdiction under the
appeal procedures provided for in the State Administrative Adjudication Act,
being I.C. 4-21.5-3-1 et seq.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.11 FREE SERVICE.
   The Council shall not grant free service or use of the storm water system to
any person, group, or entity. It is not necessary for an area or parcel of real
estate to be annexed to the town to receive storm water system services.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.12 IMPROVED LOTS; CONNECTIONS.
   Each improved lot, parcel, or user shall be obligated to use the storm water
system. Each improved lot, parcel or user may connect any pump, downspout, or
other storm water collection device in a manner that shall not permit any waste
other than rainfall or other precipitation to be placed in the system. Any and
all connections to the storm water system shall be inspected by the town prior
to their use. All connections to the storm water system shall be assessed an
inspection fee as set forth in this chapter and completed no more that 90 days
after substantial collection of the entire system and notification by the town
(“initial connection time period”). Any new or delinquent connection to the
storm water system after the initial connection time period shall be assessed a
late fee and inspection fee as per this chapter.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.13 ILLEGAL DEPOSITS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or entity to place any waste
material, oil, sludge, paint, varnish, or any other substance other than storm
water into the storm water collection system. The town may enforce this chapter
by injunction.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.14 STORM WATER TAP-IN FEE.
   The town may charge a fee for each initial connection to the storm water
system made by any property owner or other person. Said fee shall be designated
as a “storm water tap-in fee” and shall be in addition to any cost for service,
work, or materials to connect with the town’s storm water system.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
§ 53.99 PENALTY.
   Any person that shall violate this chapter may be fined in an amount not to
exceed $2,500 per violation. Each day that a violation exists shall be
considered to be a separate violation. In the event that the town shall be
required to enforce this chapter by seeking redress in the Circuit Court, the
person, firm, or entity which the enforcement action is directed shall pay all
costs associated with the enforcement action, including but not limited to,
reasonable attorney fees, court costs, witness fees, or other costs.
(Ord. 2008-4, passed 4-3-2008)
CHAPTER 54: GARBAGE
Section
   
54.01   Definitions
   
54.02   Trash collection fees
   
54.03   Delinquent payments
   
54.04   Garbage and trash regulations
 
   
54.99   Penalty
§ 54.01 DEFINITIONS.
   The terms GARBAGE and TRASH shall mean all regular household waste, but
shall not mean: tires, batteries, telephone poles, railroad ties, fuel tanks,
herbicide cans/buckets, animal carcasses, any type of medical waste, asbestos
siding and roofing shingles, any type of hazardous waste, liquid waste, empty
or full drums that have contained anything other than household waste, any item
containing Freon (refrigerators, air conditioners, and the like), and anything
containing electrical components, such as motors, computers, keyboards, and
monitors.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 4-2-2015)
§ 54.02 TRASH COLLECTION FEES.
   (A)   The town shall continue, from time to time, to contract for the
collection and disposal of trash and garbage for the benefit of the residential
dwellings, not-for-profit organizations, and small businesses within the town
limits of the town. All parties other than the above stated shall be required
and responsible for removal of their own garbage and trash, this shall
included, but not limited to, apartment complexes, trailer parks, and large
business establishments
   (B)   Each unit receiving the benefit of the town’s contractor shall be
required to pay the sum of $11.50 per month, June 1, 2021, to June 1, 2022, for
collection and disposal in order to defray the cost of the contract entered
into by the town with Best Way of America, Inc. Any additional 96 gallon trash
receptacle shall cost $4 per month for each receptacle, and the customer will
be billed directly by contractor.
   (C)   The fees provided for herein shall be payable at the same time that
the water and sewage charges are paid, and said charges shall be added to the
monthly water and sewage statement sent to each unit.
   (D)   All monies collected under this chapter shall be deposited into the
town’s Sanitation Fund.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 4-2-2015; Ord. 2017-5, passed 6-1-2017; Ord. 2021-3,
passed 6-8-2021) Penalty, see §
54.99
§ 54.03 DELINQUENT PAYMENTS.
   (A)   Failure to pay these service charges shall result in the town imposing
a 10% late charge for payments not paid in full by the fifteenth of each month.
All delinquent charges, fee, and penalties, shall become a lien on the real
estate of the owner every 90 days for any accounts which are more than 30 days
delinquent. The Town Clerk-Treasurer may certify said delinquent charges, fees,
and penalties to the real estate of the owner. A service fee may also be
assessed on the entire amount due at the time the lien is filed. All delinquent
charges, assessments, and penalties shall be payable with attorney fees and
costs of collection, and shall be payable without relief from valuation and
appraisement laws.
   (B)   If a unit is delinquent in paying its trash fees, the town shall
notify the contractor to refuse collection and disposal service to that
particular residential dweller who refuses to pay said charges. The offending
party or parties shall be notified by the Town Clerk-Treasurer, in writing, of
their delinquency and within ten days thereafter, if said delinquency is not
paid in full, collection and disposal service shall be denied to said residence
until its account is brought current.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 4-2-2015) Penalty, see §
54.99
§ 54.04 GARBAGE AND TRASH REGULATIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to dump or place any garbage or trash on any
premises in the town without the consent of the owner of such premises.
   (B)   Garbage and trash must be placed in plastic bags, which must be placed
in the trash receptacles provided to the residence, not-for-profit
organization, and small business.
   (C)   All garbage and trash must be set out within ten feet of an accessible
street as designated by the town or its authorized agent. The garbage and trash
shall be placed between the sidewalk and the curb where possible. In the event
that there is not sufficient space between the sidewalk and the curb, the
garbage and trash shall not be placed in such a manner to impede pedestrian
traffic on the sidewalk.
   (D)   Carpet must be rolled into segments not exceeding five feet in length
and each section must be no more than two feet in diameter, and placed within
the trash receptacle. Any carpet not meeting this specification will not be
removed.
   (E)   None of the following items shall be placed in any container to be
picked up in the town: tires, batteries, telephone poles, railroad ties, fuel
tanks, herbicide cans/buckets, animal carcasses, any type of medical waste,
asbestos siding and roofing shingles, any type of hazardous waste, liquid
waste, empty or full drums that have contained anything other than household
waste, any item containing Freon (refrigerators, air conditioners, and the
like), and anything containing electrical components, such as motors,
computers, keyboards, and monitors.
   (F)   No garbage or trash, or any container or receptacle containing garbage
and trash shall be set out for street pick up earlier than 6:00 p.m. on the
evening prior to the regularly scheduled collection of said garbage and trash.
Further, all receptacles which were set out for the collection of garbage and
trash shall be removed and shall not remain within 25 feet of any public street
subsequent to 6:00 p.m. on the evening of the regularly scheduled collection of
garbage and trash. Therefore, no garbage and trash, or any receptacle
containing garbage and trash, or any receptacle used primarily for the purpose
of storing garbage and trash, shall be placed in plain view within 25 feet of
any public street except during the period of time from 6:00 p.m. on the
evening prior to the scheduled collection of said garbage and trash until 6:00
p.m. of the date of the scheduled collection of said garbage and trash.
   (G)   No person, organization, institution, or other entity shall cause
garbage or trash, as defined herein, including leaves, to be deposited within
or upon the paved portion of any public street within the town.
   (H)   The town’s authorized agent will remove bulky and oversized items from
a residence once per month, which removal will be regularly scheduled each
month.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 4-2-2015) Penalty, see §
54.99
§ 54.99 PENALTY.
   Any person in violation of this chapter may be subject to a fine of up to
$1,000.
(Ord. 2015-1, passed 4-2-2015)
CHAPTER 55: GAS
Section
   
55.01   Right to enter public grounds
   
55.02   Laying of main lines
   
55.03   Plat required
   
55.04   Restoration of ground condition
   
55.05   Furnishing inhabitants
   
55.06   Charges
   
55.07   Refusal to sell; selling at higher rate than allowed
   
55.08   Rates and charges
   
55.09   Licenses and taxes
 
   
55.99   Penalty
§ 55.01 RIGHT TO ENTER PUBLIC GROUNDS.
   For the purpose of supplying the inhabitants of said town, without
discrimination, with a supply of natural gas or oil for fuel, there is granted
unto any person, firm, corporation, company, association, or individual
complying with the provisions of this chapter the privilege and right to enter
upon the streets, alleys, avenues, and public grounds of said town, and lay and
maintain therein and thereon gas lines, mains, service pipes reducing stations,
and such other appliances as may be necessary to properly equip and operate a
complete gas plant.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)
§ 55.02 LAYING OF MAIN LINES.
   Any firm, corporation, association, or individual availing themselves of the
privilege of this chapter shall lay all main lines on the improved streets at
least one foot beneath the dirt grade, and, on the unimproved streets, at least
two feet beneath the dirt grade, and shall, at their own expense, furnish and
lay to the curb of the gutter service pipes not less than one inch in diameter,
and shall equip the consumer’s end of the service pipe with a first class stop
cock and service box so as to permit the gas to be readily shut off. Such mains
and service pipes shall be so laid as not to interfere with the existing
drainage in said town. If, at any time in the future, the construction,
alteration, or repair of any street shall necessitate the charge of any main or
lines laid under this grant; then, upon five days notice in writing from the
said Town Council, any firm, corporation, or individual availing themselves of
the privilege of this chapter shall immediately proceed to take up and change
said mains and lines so as to correspond with the requirements of the said Town
Council.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.03 PLAT REQUIRED.
   (A)   Before any firm, corporation, or individual avail themselves of the
privilege of this chapter, they shall first file with the Town Council of said
town a plat showing the location of any lines heretofore laid, of all lines
that they may hereafter propose to lay, setting out in said plat the streets
along which said lines are laid or along which said lines are laid or along
which they are proposed to be laid and the side of the street where the lines
are laid or where they are proposed to be laid, which said plat shall be
approved by the Town Council and kept as a public record. And the Town Council
shall have the right to make such changes in any proposed lines as the public
interest may, in their judgment, require. They shall also file with the Town
Council a bond in the penal sum of $1,000 with good and sufficient sureties
conditioned that they will comply with all of the terms and conditions of this
chapter on their part, and that they will fully indemnify, hold, and save
harmless the said town from any and all damages growing out of the construction
of said plant, or growing out of anything done or the failure to do anything
required by this chapter, and that they will defeud the said town against any
and all suits that may be brought against the said town on account of anything
done or performed or the failure to do or perform anything required by the
provisions of this chapter.
   (B)   Before any firm, corporation, or individual shall avail themselves of
the provisions of this chapter, they shall first file with the Town Council of
said town the plat and bond herein before set out and shall in addition thereto
file with the said Town Council a written acceptance by which all of the terms
and conditions of this chapter will be fully and fairly complied with.
   (C)   Before any corporation or company shall avail itself of the provisions
of this chapter, it shall file with the Town Clerk-Treasurer its written
acceptance of all the provisions of this chapter, which acceptance shall be
signed by the president and secretary of such corporation or company with a
certified copy of a resolution duly passed by the board of directors of such
corporation authorizing the execution and filing thereof, accepting all the
provisions of this chapter. If a firm or individual desires to furnish gas
under the provisions of this chapter such firm or individual shall likewise
file his, her, or their written acceptance in the same words substantially, and
upon the same terms provided for corporations or companies as provided in this
section.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.04 RESTORATION OF GROUND CONDITION.
   Any firm, corporation, or individual availing themselves of the privileges
of this chapter shall restore all streets, alleys, avenues, and public grounds
disturbed by them in the laying of their mains or doing the work under this
chapter to as good condition as they were before the commencement of the work
and so maintain that part of the streets so disturbed in good condition for one
year. Whenever any gravel or improved street shall be opened for the purpose of
laying any mains or service pipes, the gravel, or other material placed upon
the dirt grade shall be placed upon one side of the trench and the dirt
excavated shall be placed upon the opposite side, and when filled in, the dirt
shall be tamped thoroughly in, first, and the gravel then placed in on top of
the dirt, and after any street or alley has been dug into or disturbed for the
purpose of laying such pipes, the parts so disturbed shall be maintained in
good condition for the period of one year thereafter.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.05 FURNISHING INHABITANTS.
   As a further condition to the exercise of this franchise and in
consideration of the privileges granted by the said town, any firm,
corporation, or individual availing themselves of the privileges of this
chapter agree that they will furnish to the inhabitants of said town without
discrimination an abundant supply of gas or oil for fuel, and that they will
maintain for the consumers in the service mains along the streets of said town
a pressure of at least eight ounces at the POINT OF CONSUMPTION which is
defined to be the point at which the gas is delivered from the lines and
service pipes of the company to the consumers.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)
§ 55.06 CHARGES.
   All companies, corporations, persons, firms, associations, and individuals
operating a plant and furnishing natural gas under the provisions of this
chapter shall charge for natural gas provided by this chapter and for each
stove, grate, light, and furnace from and after the time that such stove,
grate, light, and furnace shall have been attached for use of gas upon the
application of the consumer and not from any anterior date or time.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)
§ 55.07 REFUSAL TO SELL; SELLING AT HIGHER RATE THAN ALLOWED.
   Any person or persons, firm, corporation, company, individual, or
association or any officer, agent, clerk, or employer, of such person, or
persons, firm, corporation, company, individual, or association who shall
refuse to sell, furnish, or supply natural gas to any inhabitant of this town
to be used for light or fuel or shall ask, charge, exact, demand, take, or
receive a larger sum, greater value, or prive for natural gas for light or fuel
than allowed and fixed by this chapter, or shall cause natural gas to flow
through their service pipes to consumers at the point of consumption within the
corporate limits of said town at a pressure less than eight ounces to the
square inch or shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
fined and forfeit to the said town, for each offense any sum not to exceed $10
for each offense.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)
§ 55.08 RATES AND CHARGES.
   In consideration of the use of the streets, alleys, avenues, and public
grounds of this town for the granting of merchandise, all persons, firms,
corporations, companies, individuals, and associations availing themselves of
the rights under this chapter shall as a condition of the exercise of the
franchises therein granted furnish within the limits of said town, natural gas
to consumers for and at a price not to exceed the rates set out in the
following schedule to-wit:
Business rooms
   Monthly charges from November 1 to May 1 next each year
      No. 5 mixer, each per month                                        $3
      No. 4 mixer, each per month                                        $2.50
   Monthly charges for May and October each year
      No. 5 mixer, per month $1.50
      No. 4 mixer, per month $1.25
Domestic
   Monthly charges from November 1 to May 1, each year
      Cooking stove, No. 7 mixer, each per month                         $2.25
      Cooking stove, No. 5 mixer, each per month                         $2
      Cooking stove, No. 4 mixer, each per month                         $1.75
   In winter when a cooking stove only is used, the price to be the same as
for heating stoves for like mixer
Furnaces
   Monthly charges from November 1 to May 1 next each year
      No. 7 mixer, each per month                                        $3.15
      No. 5 mixer, each per month                                        $2.50
Heating stoves and grates
   Monthly charges from November 1 to May 1 each year
      First No. 7 mixer, each per month                                  $2.60

§ 55.09 LICENSES AND TAXES.
   The town expressly reserves the right at any time after the passage of this
chapter to require any company corporation, firm, or individual furnishing gas
under the provision of this chapter as a further condition and consideration to
this grant and franchise to pay into the Town Treasury annually on January 1
beginning each year a license or tax not exceeding one-half of $0.01 per foot
of mains laid by such corporation, company, firm, or individual within the town
limits, exclusive of service pipes.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)
§ 55.99 PENALTY.
   Any firm, corporation, or individual availing themselves of the privileges
of this chapter who shall violate any of the terms and conditions of this
chapter shall be fined in a sum not to exceed $10 and each and every day the
violation of any of the provisions of this chapter shall continue, shall be any
constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 52, passed 11-6-1901)

CHAPTER 70: TRAFFIC RULES
Section
   
70.01   Speed limits generally
   
70.02   Disorderly conduct by motor vehicles
   
70.03   Driving on curb stone
 
   
70.99   Penalty
§ 70.01 SPEED LIMITS GENERALLY.
   It is unlawful for any person or persons, to move or caused to be moved, or
propelled or driven any automobile, truck, bus, motorcycle, or any other motor
powered machine, upon the streets or alley, within the corporation limits of
said town, at any greater rate of speed than 25 mph.
(Ord. 110, passed 4-17-1941) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.02 DISORDERLY CONDUCT BY MOTOR VEHICLES.
   No person, firm, or corporation shall operate or cause to be operated a
motor vehicle on the streets or public highways of the town, in such manner or
with such equipment as to make, create, facilitate, increase or maintain any
loud, unnecessary, excessive, or unusual noise which either annoys, disturbs,
injures, or endangers the comfort, repose, or peace and quiet of any other
person or of any neighborhood within the town.
(Ord. 132, passed 8-2-1971; Ord. 2000-6, passed 4-27-2000) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.03 DRIVING ON CURB STONE.
   It shall be unlawful for any one to drive across the curb stone on Kain
Street.
(Ord. 16, passed - -) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person, agent, employee, or owner of said machine, found violating
any provision of §
70.01, shall upon conviction, for each and every such offense, forfeit and pay
to the said town any sum of money not exceeding $25.
   (C)   Any person, firm, or corporation violating §
70.02 shall guilty of a Class B infraction and shall be subject to a fine in a
sum not exceeding $1,000.
   (D)   The fine for violating §
70.03 shall not exceed the sum of $3 for each offense.
(Ord. 16, passed - -; Ord. 110, passed 4-17-1941; Ord. 132, passed 8-2-1971;
Ord. 2000-6, passed 4-27-2000)
CHAPTER 71: PARKING RULES
Section
General Provisions
   
71.01   Blocking of alleys
   
71.02   Curb parking
   
71.03   Freight curb loading zones
Truck Parking
   
71.15   Definition
   
71.16   Unlawful parking
   
71.17   Notice of violation
 
   
71.99   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 71.01 BLOCKING OF ALLEYS.
   No person shall park any vehicle or place any materials in an alley in such
a manner or under such conditions as would leave available less than ten feet
of the width of the alley for the free movement of traffic.
(Ord. 1992-4, passed 9-8-1992) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.02 CURB PARKING.
   There shall be flat parking with the curb upon all streets within the town.
(Ord. 115-1956, passed 5-1-1956) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 FREIGHT CURB LOADING ZONES.
   (A)   The Town Council may designate or assign freight curb loading zones
upon request by any person provided the person makes application for a permit
for the freight curb loading zone and for two signs to indicate the ends of the
freight curb loading zone.
   (B)   (1)   The Town Council may attach any restrictions to the use of the
freight curb loading zone it deems appropriate.
      (2)   Restrictions may include, but are not limited to, times of loading
or unloading, types of vehicles allowed to use the freight curb loading zone,
and/or length of time a vehicle may remain in the freight curb loading zone.
   (C)   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall collect from the person making the
application a one time service fee equal to the cost and installation of the
signs.
   (D)   (1)   In addition, the Clerk-Treasurer shall collect an annual fee of
$25 over and above the cost of the sign.
      (2)   The first annual fee is due on the anniversary date of the approval
of the freight curb loading zone.
      (3)   If the applicant fails to make an annual fee payment, the freight
curb loading zone permit may be revoked and the signs removed.
   (E)   Every permit is subject to revocation by the Town Council at anytime
for any cause or reason, including but not limited to, the failure to comply
with all restrictions placed upon the freight curb loading zone.
(Ord. 5, passed 9-8-1992) Penalty, see §
71.99
TRUCK PARKING
§ 71.15 DEFINITION.
   For the purposes of this subchapter, a TRUCK shall be defined as all or any
part of a vehicle whose combined length is in excess of 24 feet, whose combined
weight is more than three tons and which is designed or operated for the
transportation of property, i.e., commonly referred to as a semi trailer or
semi tractor and trailer.
(Ord. 1988-1, passed 2-10-1988)
§ 71.16 UNLAWFUL PARKING.
   It shall be unlawful and a violation of this subchapter for any truck to
stop or stand in the traveled portion of roadway, or to stop or park next to
the curb, for a period of time longer than one hour.
(Ord. 1988-1, passed 2-10-1988) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.17 NOTICE OF VIOLATION.
   It shall be the duty of the police officers of the town to attach to a
vehicle a notice to the owner or operator thereof that the vehicle has been
parked in violation of the parking ordinances of the town and instructing the
owner or operator to report at the office of the Police Department of the town
in regard to the violation.
(Ord. 1988-1, passed 2-10-1988)
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   The owner of any motor vehicle who violates §
71.01 shall be fined not less than $5 nor more than $50 for each offense.
   (C)   Any person, firm, or corporation violating any of the provisions of §
71.02 shall upon conviction be fined in any sum not exceeding $10 for any one
offense.
   (D)   Each such owner or operator in violation of any parking ordinances of
this town, shall, within 24 hours of the time when the notice was attached to
the vehicle, pay to the Police Department as a penalty for and in full
satisfaction of the violation, the sum of $25, Any such owner or operator who
shall have a second violation of the parking ordinances of the town shall,
within 24 hours of the time when the notice was attached to the vehicle, pay to
the Police Department as a penalty for and in full satisfaction of the
violation, the sum of $35. Each such owner or operator who shall have received
three or more violations shall be cited into the town court and fined not less
than $250.
(Ord. 115-1956, passed 5-1-1956; Ord. 1988-1, passed 2-10-1988; Ord. 1992-4,
passed 9-8-1992)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 72.01 RIDING AND DRIVING ON SIDEWALKS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to ride or drive upon any cement
sidewalk for the use of foot passengers, within the corporate limits, of the
town except to pass over the same upon a provided crossing.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, drive, or propel, upon
any cement sidewalk within the corporate limits of the town, any sled, roller
skates, or skates of any kind, bicycle, tricycle, large or small wagon,
vehicle, or any conveyance or vehicle of any kind except what is known as a
stroller, whether so used for exercise, business, or pleasure, except to cross
over the same at provided crossings.
(Ord. 78, passed 4-28-1908) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.02 SKATEBOARDS, ROLLER BLADES, AND ROLLER SKATES.
   Skateboards, roller blades and roller skates, shall be banned from the area
known as Uptown Parker City, including 50 feet North of Howard Street on Main
Street going south to the alley on the south side of the post office, includes
both sides of Main Street including the sidewalks.
(Ord. 2006-2, passed 5-4-2006) Penalty, see §
72.99
GOLF CARTS
§ 72.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid current license to operate a motor vehicle issued
by Indiana or any other state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability insurance coverage on a golf cart in an
amount not less that required by state law for motor vehicles operated on
public highways in the state.
   GOLF CART. Shall have the definition provided in I.C. 9-13-2-69.7. As it now
exists, that term means: a four-wheeled motor vehicle originally and
specifically designed and intended to transport one or more individuals and
golf clubs for the purpose of playing the game of golf on a golf course.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012)
§ 72.16 OPERATION OF GOLF CART.
   The operation of a golf cart on streets within the town is strictly
prohibited unless the golf cart is operated and equipped in full compliance
with this subchapter.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.17 OPERATOR.
   Only persons over 16 years of age and holding a valid, current driver’s
license may operate a golf cart.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.18 FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY PROOF.
   (A)   The operator of a golf cart must show financial responsibility when
operating a golf cart.
   (B)   Written proof of financial responsibility must be available either on
the golf cart or carried by the operator at all times.
   (C)   The owner must obtain and have installed at all times before operating
a valid inspection sticker as described in this subchapter.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.19 TIME OF OPERATION.
   Golf carts shall not be operated on town streets during one-half hour after
sunset to one-half hour before sunrise unless the golf cart is equipped with
two operating headlights (one on each side of the front of the golf cart) and
two operating tail lights with brake lights (one on each side of the rear of
the golf cart) which are visible from a distance of 500 feet.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.20 PLACE OF OPERATION.
   (A)   Golf carts may be operated on town streets which have a posted speed
limit of 30 mph or less.
   (B)   Golf carts may not be operated on sidewalks or State Road 32 and may
only cross State Road 32.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.21 OCCUPANTS.
   (A)   The number of occupants in a golf cart shall be limited to the number
of persons for whom factory seating is installed and provided on the golf cart.
   (B)   The operator and all occupants shall be seated in the golf cart and no
part of the body of the operator or occupant shall extend outside the perimeter
of the golf cart while the golf cart is being operated.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.22 TRAFFIC RULES.
   The operator of the golf cart shall comply with all traffic rules and
regulations adopted by the state and the town which govern the operation of
motor vehicles.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.23 SLOW MOVING VEHICLE SIGN.
   All golf carts must display on the back of the golf cart a “slow moving
vehicle” emblem in accordance with I.C. 9-21-1-3 and, if operated after dark or
before dawn, the equipment described in §
72.19.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.24 SPEED LIMIT.
   No golf cart shall be operated at a speed in excess of 25 mph irrespective
of posted speed limit. In the event any posted speed limit is less than 25 mph,
the posted speed limit shall be the maximum.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.25 SAFETY EQUIPMENT.
   All golf carts shall be equipped with brakes as specified in I.C. 9-19-3-1.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.26 PARKING.
   Parking of golf carts shall be in designated area for parking of golf carts
or motor vehicles. No parking on sidewalks or tree lawns.
(Ord. 2012-2, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
MOTORIZED VEHICLES
§ 72.40 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MOPED. 
      (1)   Any two- or three-wheeled vehicle that is propelled by an internal
combustion engine or a battery-powered motor, or by both, and is powered by an
internal combustion engine, has the following:
         (a)   An engine rating of not more than two horsepower and a cylinder
capacity not exceeding 50 cubic centimeters;
         (b)   An automatic transmission; and
         (c)   A maximum design speed of no more than 25 mph on a flat surface.
      (2)   The term SCOOTER shall be interchangeable with the term MOPED.
      (3)   Specifically excluded from the definition of MOPED are the
following:
         (a)   Any two- or three-wheeled vehicle exceeding the above
specifications and deemed to be a motorcycle required to be registered with and
by a state bureau of motor vehicles;
         (b)   An electric personal assistance mobility device presently
defined in I.C. 9-13-2-49.3; and
         (c)   An off-road vehicle, otherwise known as all terrain vehicle
(ATV), presently defined in I.C. 14-8-2-185, and required to be registered by
the Department of Natural Resources under I.C. 14-16-1 et seq.
   POCKET BIKE. Also referred to as a POCKET ROCKET, shall mean any wheeled
device ridden by a person for use as transportation, powered or assisted by any
on-board power source other than the rider’s own physical efforts that has a
handlebar height of 30 inches or less, measured from the highest point of the
handlebar, or a seat height of 24 inches or less, as measured from the highest
point of the horizontal seat surface actually designed to bear the weight of
the rider. Specifically excluded from the definition of POCKET BIKE are the
following:
      (1)   Any two- or three-wheeled vehicle deemed to be a motorcycle
required to be registered with and by a state Bureau of Motor Vehicles;
      (2)   An electric personal assistance mobility device presently defined
in I.C. 9-13-2-49.3; and
      (3)   An off-road vehicle, otherwise known as al-terrain vehicle (ATV),
presently defined in I.C. 14-8-2-185, and required to be registered by the
Department of Natural Resources under I.C. 14-16-1 et seq.
   ROADWAY. Any highway road, public way, street, parking lot, or alley and
shall include any street designated as a parkway, boulevard, place, avenue, or
other similar designation, all of which are within the town corporate limits.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012)
§ 72.41 EFFECT OF REGULATIONS.
   (A)   It is a violation for any person to do any act forbidden or fail to
perform any act required in this subchapter. This subchapter shall apply to the
town residents and shall apply to non-residents who operate mopeds or pocket
bikes within the town corporate limits.
   (B)   The parent or guardian of any child under the age of 18 shall not
authorize or knowingly permit any child or ward to violate any of the provision
of this subchapter.
   (C)   This subchapter is applicable to mopeds and pocket bikes and shall
apply whenever a moped or pocket bike is operated on any and all roadways,
streets, alleys, sidewalks, parking lots, and public ways within the town or on
any path set aside for the exclusive use of mopeds within the town subject to
those exceptions or prohibitions stated herein.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.42 APPLICATION TO STATE TRAFFIC LAWS; OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC DEVICES.
   (A)   Every person riding a moped on a roadway in the town shall be subject
to all of the duties applicable to the driver or operator of a vehicle by the
laws of this state declaring sections of the road applicable to vehicles or by
the traffic ordinances of this town applicable to the driver of a vehicle, in
addition to special regulations in this subchapter and except as to those
provisions of laws and ordinances which by their nature can have no
application. An person disobeying the traffic control devices or signs, or
violating state statutes while operating a moped shall receive a state
citation.
   (B)   A moped must not be operated:
      (1)   By a person less than 15 years of age;
      (2)   By a person who has not obtained a state-issued identification card
or operator’s license;
      (3)   On an interstate highway or a sidewalk; or
      (4)   At a speed greater then 25 mph.
   (C)   A police officer having probable cause to believe a person has
violated division (B)(1) or (B)(2) above may immediately impound the moped as
evidence and hold it until a court of competent jurisdiction resolves any
enforcement action filed. If no action has been filed in court to enforce the
violation of this section, the Police Department shall allow the owner to
retrieve the moped bicycle within 45 days of its seizure.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012)
§ 72.43 ALTERATION RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The owner, if 18 years of age or older, or the parent or guardian of a
minor, who is the owner of a moped shall not alter or allow the alteration of
the OEM exhaust system which permits loud exhaust.
   (B)   An owner, if 18 years of age or older, or the parent or guardian of a
minor, who owns a moped with an engine that has been manufactured, converted,
modified, or altered to the degree that the moped qualifies as a motorcycle
under state law (where the engine rating exceeds more than two horsepower, the
cylinder capacity exceeds more than 50 cubic centimeters, or the maximum design
speed exceeds 25 mph on a flat surface shall be required to:
      (1)   Properly register, license, and insure said vehicle as a motorcycle
pursuant to state law (presently I.C. 9-18.1-2-3) or shall be required to
properly register, license, and insure said vehicle as a privately assembled
vehicle pursuant to state law (presently I.C. 9-17-4 et seq.); and
      (2)   Shall be required to hold a state-issued motorcycle operator’s
license or endorsement pursuant to state law (presently I.C. 9-24-8 et seq.).
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012)
§ 72.44 OPERATION, PASSENGERS, SAFETY, AND PARKING.
   (A)   Every person operating a moped on a roadway shall ride as near to the
right side of the roadway as practicable, exercising due care when passing a
standing vehicle or one proceeding in the same direction.
   (B)   No moped shall be operated on a sidewalk or a railroad right-of-way.
   (C)   No moped shall be operated on another’s private property, unless the
express written consent has been obtained from the owner of the real estate or
unless written notice has been posted on the private real estate.
   (D)   No person shall operate a moped in a manner so as to create loud
unnecessary or unusual noise so as to disturb or interfere with the peace and
quiet of other persons.
   (E)   A person operating a moped shall not ride other than astride a
permanent and regular seat attached thereto. A passenger on a moped shall not
ride other then astride a permanent and regular seat attached thereto. All
persons operating or riding as a passenger must be able to keep his or her feet
firmly on the foot boards or foot pegs while sitting comfortably on the seat or
saddle.
   (F)   No moped shall be used to carry more persons at one time then the
number for which it is designed and equipped, as designed with an additional
set of foot boards or foot pegs.
   (G)   No moped shall be used to carry any child under the age of 15 years.
   (H)   No person shall operate a moped at a speed that is greater than
reasonable and prudent under the conditions then existing, In no case shall a
person operate a moped at a speed greater than 25 mph.
   (I)   The operator of a moped emerging from an alley, driveway, or building
shall on approaching a sidewalk area extending across any alleyway, yield the
right-of-way to all pedestrians approaching on the sidewalk or sidewalk area,
and on entering the roadway shall yield the right-of-way to all vehicles
approaching on the roadway.
   (J)   No person shall propel or operate a moped in any unsafe manner,
including, but not limited to weaving or swerving over the road, cutting
through traffic, excessive lane changes, following other vehicles too closely,
excessive or dangerous acceleration, or jumping curbs or speed bumps.
   (K)   Both wheels of all mopeds must be on the surface being ridden upon at
all times such moped is in operation.
   (L)   Persons operating mopeds shall pull over and allow traffic to pass in
the event two or more vehicles are backed up behind the mopeds.
   (M)   No person shall car any package, bundle, or article which prevents the
rider from keeping all hands on the handlebars.
   (N)   No person shall park a moped on a street other then on the roadway
against the curb or against a building or at the curb, in such a manner as to
afford the least obstruction to pedestrian traffic.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.45 MOPED REGISTRATION AND INSPECTION.
   (A)   The owner, if 18 years or older, or the parent or guardian of a minor
who is the owner, of a moped, who resides within the town may have the moped
registered with the Police Department.
   (B)   These provisions shall apply any time there is a change of ownership,
including those instances when the moped has been registered to the previous
owner.
   (C)   Registration shall include the imprinting, stamping, or otherwise
placing of a registration number on each moped and the keeping of appropriate
records by the Police Department as to identification of the mopeds and their
ownership.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012)
§ 72.46 EQUIPMENT AND PROPER IDENTIFICATION.
   (A)   (1)   Every moped when in use at night shall be equipped with a front
lamp which shall emit a white light visible from a distance of at least 500
feet to the front and with a red reflector on the rear of a type which shall be
visible from all distances from 50 feet to 300 feet to the rear when directly
in front of lawful upper beams of headlamps on a motor vehicle.
      (2)   A lamp emitting a red light visible from a distance of 500 feet to
the rear may be used in addition to the red reflector.
   (B)   A person less than 18 years of age who operates a moped or rides a
moped as a passenger, on a street or highway shall wear protective headgear,
and must also wear protective glasses, goggles, or a transparent face shield,
as set forth in I.C. 9-21-11-13.
   (C)   A person less than 18 years of age who operates a moped shall enroll
in a motorcycle driver education and training course, may be required to at the
recommendation of the Winchester City Court, prior to operation of the moped on
town roadways.
   (D)   An adult operating a moped shall carry the identification required
pursuant to §
72.42 and I.C. 9-21-11-12 when operating the moped, and shall, when detained by
a police officer, produce said identification to the police officer.
   (E)   A person operating a moped that has not yet been registered pursuant
to §
72.45 shall carry either the moped registration paperwork or the dated sales
receipt during the initial 30 days of ownership, and shall, when detained by a
police officer, produce said paperwork and/or sales receipt to the police
officer.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.47 RENTAL AGENCIES.
   (A)   A rental agency shall not rent or offer any moped for rent unless the
moped is equipped with the lamps and other equipment required in this
subchapter.
   (B)   A rental agency shall not rent or offer any moped for rent to anyone
under the age of 15 years of age.
   (C)   A rental agency shall not rent or offer any moped for rent to any
minor between the age of 15 and 18 years of age unless:
      (1)   The minor has identification required pursuant to §
72.42 and I.C. 9-21-11-12; and
      (2)   The minor’s parent or guardian signs the rental agreement.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.48 POCKET BIKES.
   (A)   The use of pocket bikes is prohibited on any and all roadways,
streets, alleys, sidewalks, and public ways within the town.
   (B)   In addition of the above prohibition on the use of pocket bikes as set
forth in division (A) above, any person who owns or operates a pocket bike
shall also be required to comply with the entirety of this subchapter as it
applies to mopeds with the exception that pocket bikes are not required to be
registered. In the event any person commits a violation of the provisions of
this subchapter while operating a pocket bike, that person shall be fined under
§
72.99 for the specific violation, or shall be fined for the state violation, in
addition to the penalty for operation of the prohibited pocket bike.
(Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-5, passed 5-3-2012) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate §
72.01, or any provisions of divisions (A) and (B) of that section, or either of
them, shall be fined, in the sum not less than $1, nor more than $10, for each
offense thereof.
   (C)   For violations of §
72.02:
      (1)   For the first offense, the town police officers have the option of:
         (a)   Warning the individual or individuals; or
         (b)   Impounding the roller blades, skateboard, or roller skates until
which time a parent has a meeting with individual and officer.
      (2)   For the second offense, a citation will be issued to the parent if
the person committing the offense is a juvenile. If an adult, a citation will
be issued.
      (3)   The fines for violation of §
72.02 are as follows:
         (a)   For the first offense is up to $10 and court cost; and
         (b)   Second offense is up to $50 and court cost.
   (D)   Anyone violating any of the provisions of §§
71.15 to
72.26 shall be subject to a fine of $25 for the first violation, $50 for the
second violation, and $75 for the third violation. If a person is cited for a
violation of §§
72.15 to
72.26 more than three times, the registration shall be revoked and said golf
cart shall no longer be allowed to operate on streets, roads, or alley within
the town. The fee(s) are to be paid to the Violations Bureau.
   (E)   (1)   Any person, firm, or corporation who violates any provision of
§§
72.40 to
72.48 for which another penalty is not specifically provided, shall, upon
conviction, be subject to a fine not exceeding $2,500. A separate offense shall
be deemed committed upon each day during which a violation occurs or continues.
(I.C. 36-1-3-8(a)10)
      (2)   Anyone violating any of the provisions of §§
72.40 to
72.48 shall be subject to a fine of a minimum $25, up to a maximum of $100 for
each citation. The fee(s) are to be paid to the Violations Bureau.
      (3)   (a)   A police officer having probable cause to believe a person
has violated any provision of this chapter may immediately confiscate the
motorized vehicle or pocket bike and remove it to a garage or other place of
safety as designated by the Police Department. Whenever an officer removes a
motorized vehicle or pocket bike as authorized under this division (E)(3), the
officer shall enter such fact on the records of the Police Department
maintained for such purpose, and the records shall be kept to show the type of
vehicle, name of the registered owner, license number, and the name and address
of the operator of the vehicle as the time it became impounded, if such
information is available to the officer. Thereafter, on the request of the
owner of any such vehicle for its return, the Police Department shall issue an
order directing the owner or his or her agents or representatives to pay all
charges incurred as a result of the vehicle being towed to a place of safety.
         (b)   For purposes of this division (E)(3), the Town Council finds
that there is a compelling governmental interest in imposing the following
discretionary penalty section for minor children, in order to encourage
parental intervention and responsibility for the violations of the minor
children. The town further finds that impoundment is more likely to prevent
repeat offenses by minors than the imposition of monetary penalties. In lieu of
the penalty described in this division (E)(3)(b), any police officer may, in
his or her discretion, utilize the following penalty provision for violations
by minor children.
            1.   First offense. With the child’s first offense in a 365-day
period, the town shall issue a written warning and notification of the
violation to the child’s parent or guardian.
            2.   Second offense. With the child’s second offense in a 365-day
period, the town shall issue a written notice of violation, and the
investigating officer may take custody of the motorized vehicle or pocket bike,
and hold the same for safekeeping for 60 days, or until the child’s parent or
guardian claims the motorized vehicle or pocket bike. The child’s parent or
guardian shall be responsible for any charges incurred by the town for
impounding the motorized vehicle or pocket bike, including, but not limited to,
towing and storage.
            3.   Third and subsequent offenses. With the child’s third offense
in a 365-day period, the town shall include a civil fine, not to exceed $100.
The arresting officer may take custody of the motorized vehicle or pocket bike,
and hold the same for safekeeping for 60 days. An officer, or his or her
superior, may waive the imposed civil fine and/or impoundment if the parent and
child agree to the child attending and completing a motorized vehicle safety
course.
(Ord. 78, passed 4-28-1908; Ord. 2006-2, passed 5-4-2006; Ord. 2012-2, passed
4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-3, passed 4-5-2012; Ord. 2012-4, passed 5-3-2012; Ord.
2012-5, passed 5-3-2012)

SCHEDULE II. DIRECTION OF TRAFFIC.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this schedule, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      TRAFFIC FLOW. The direction of movement of a vehicle.
      TRAFFIC FLOW SIGNS AND MARKINGS. Any sign, signal, or device of
sufficient size and markings to give notice to the user, driver, or operator of
a vehicle of the regulated traffic flow.
      VEHICLE. Any device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or
may be transported upon a public highway. The definition of VEHICLE shall
include, but not be limited to, the following: motor vehicle, car, truck,
motorcycle, tractor, bus, motor home, motor camper, snowmobile, van, jeep,
motorized farm equipment, moped, and motor bicycle.
   (B)   One-way traffic north only. The traffic flow on the following
described alley situated in the town shall be one-way north only, said alley
being more particularly described as follows, to-wit:
      (1)   Being a part of Block Three in the original plat of the Town of
Morristown, now Parker City, Indiana, and commencing at the northeast corner of
Lot Five of said Block Three and running thence east approximately 16 and one-
half feet to the northwest corner of Lot Four of said Block Three; thence
running south along the west line of Lots Four and Three of said Block Three
approximately 132 feet to the southwest corner of said Lot Three of said Block;
thence running west approximately 16 and one-half feet to the southeast corner
of Lot Six of said Block Three; thence running north along the east line of
Lots Six and Five of said Block Three approximately 132 feet to the place of
beginning; and
      (2)   Said alley being located immediately south of Howard Street and
being the first north-south alley immediately east of Main Street in Parker
City, Indiana.
   (C)   Installation of traffic flow signs and markings. The Street
Commissioner of the town shall cause to be installed at appropriate locations
on said described alley appropriate traffic flow signs and markings designating
the traffic flow on said alley to be one-way north only.
   (D)   Violations. It shall be unlawful and a violation of the provisions of
this schedule for any person, firm, or corporation to drive, use, or operate or
to cause to be driven, used or operated, any vehicle in a south direction on
said aforedescribed alley or to drive, use, or operate or to cause to be
driven, used, or operated any vehicle on said aforedescribed alley in any
manner contrary to the provisions of this schedule and/or contrary to
appropriate traffic flow signs and markings erected pursuant to division (C)
above.
   (E)   Penalties. If any person, firm, or corporation shall violate the
provisions of this schedule, for each such violation, each such person, firm,
or corporation commits a Class C infraction, and shall be fined not more than
$500.
(Ord. 139, passed 3-18-1981)
 SCHEDULE III. LOADING ZONES.
   (A)   There is established a loading zone on the north side of Howard
Street, commencing at a point where the west line of an alley running a general
north-south direction on and along the west line of Lots 1, 2, 3, and 4 in
Block 5 of the original plat of the Town of Parker City, Indiana, intersects
with the north line of Howard Street, running thence east along the north line
of Howard Street a distance of 40 feet, funning thence south 33 feet to the
center of Howard Street, thence west along the center of Howard Street to a
point 33 feet north of the point where said alley intersects the north line of
Howard Street, thence running north to the place of beginning.
   (B)   A LOADING ZONE, for the purposes of this schedule, is defined as an
area wherein a public or private carrier may between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and
12:00 a.m. Monday through Saturday of each calendar week be parked for a period
of time not to exceed 15 minutes for the purpose of loading and unloading
consumer goods, merchandise, and supplies as are used in wholesale and retail
business and furniture, fixtures, appliances, and machinery as may be necessary
or desirable for use in a retail or wholesale business establishment.
   (C)   The curb on the north side of Howard Street constituting the north
line of said loading zone shall be painted yellow and there shall be erected
signs advising the general public of the existence of such loading zone, and
that during the hours from 8:00 a.m. until 12:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday
of each calendar week, there is no parking in the same except for carriers,
public and private, of consumer goods.
   (D)   It shall be unlawful to permit any vehicle, other than carriers,
public and private, of consumer goods, to stand in said loading zone except
when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the
directions of a police officer.
   (E)   Any person violating any of the terms of this schedule shall, upon
conviction of such violation, be fined in a sum of not less than $5 nor more
than $25.
(Ord. 133, passed 11-15-1976)
SCHEDULE IV. PARKING.
   (A)   Truck parking.
      (1)   The town prohibits the parking of vehicles in excess of 9,000
pounds gross vehicle license tag weight on Franklin Street beginning at the 200
block south proceeding south and ending at South Street.
      (2)   Exceptions to the prohibition of vehicles in excess of 9,000 pound
gross vehicle weight may be allowed by the Town Council through the approval of
an application for a freight curb loading zone.
      (3)   The owner of any motor vehicle who violates this division (A) shall
be fined not less than $25 nor more than $100.
