GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL. Any living, nonhuman vertebrate creature.
   AT LARGE. An animal which is not confined without means of escape in a pen,
corral, yard, cage, house, vehicle, or other secure enclosure, unless the
animal is otherwise under control of a competent human being.
   CRIME PREVENTION ANIMAL. An animal trained and used primarily by its owner
or keeper for the protection of persons or property, or both.
   EXPOSED TO RABIES. An animal has been exposed to rabies if it has been
bitten by or been in contact with any animal known or reasonably suspected to
have been infected with rabies.
   KENNEL. A facility, operated commercially and principally for the purpose of
boarding, housing, grooming, breeding, or training dogs or cats, or both. A
KENNEL, for purposes of this chapter, shall not include a facility in or
adjoining a private residence where dogs are kept for the hobby of the
householder, using them for hunting, practice, tracking, exhibiting in shows or
field or obedience trails, or for the guarding or protecting of the
householder’s property, and an occasional sale of puppies by the owner, lessee,
or other occupant of such property shall not make that property a KENNEL.
   OWN. To keep, harbor, or have custody, charge, or control of an animal.
OWNER shall include any person who owns the animal. Veterinarians, operators of
kennels, pet shops, and stables temporarily keeping animals owned by or held
for sale to other persons shall not be deemed, for the purposes of this
chapter, to own or be OWNERS, but rather “keepers” of animals.
   PET. An animal obtained or kept by its owner solely for purposes of
enjoyment, companionship, safety, or other noncommercial purposes.
   VETERINARIANS. A person licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the
state.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.002 APPLICABILITY TO NONRESIDENT DOG AND CAT OWNERS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the owner or keeper of an animal to cause,
suffer, or allow that animal which is owned or kept by him or her to be at
large within the town.
   (B)   ANIMAL NUISANCE is created when an animal:
      (1)   Molests or disturbs persons or vehicles by chasing, barking, or
biting;
      (2)   Barks, whines, howls, meows, cries, or makes other noises
excessively;
      (3)   Creates noxious or offensive odors;
      (4)   Defecates upon any public place or upon premises not owned by,
controlled by the owner or keeper unless promptly removed by the animal owner
or keeper; and/or
      (5)   Creates an insect breeding and/or attraction site due to an
accumulation of excreta.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.003 CONFINEMENT OF FEMALE ANIMALS IN HEAT.
   All female animals in heat shall be confined in a secure enclosure and in
such a manner as not to become a nuisance.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.004 VICIOUS DOGS TO BE CONFINED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for an owner or keeper of vicious, fierce, or
dangerous dog to cause, suffer, or allow it to go unconfined and unrestrained
on his or her premises, or to run at large.
   (B)   For purposes of this section, a VICIOUS, FIERCE, OR DANGEROUS DOG
means any dog which has:
      (1)   Attacked a person without having been provoked by that person;
      (2)   Attacked, at some place other than its owner’s property, another
animal; or
      (3)   Chased or approached a person at some place other than its owner’s
property, in a menacing fashion or apparent attitude of attack.
   (C)   It shall be the duty of any person having authority to impound a dog
forthwith to impound any such dog found unconfined or running at large in
violation of this section.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.005 ANNOYING DOGS.
   (A)   No person shall own, harbor, or keep in custody a dog which disturbs
the peace by barking, yelping, howling, or making other loud noises to the
annoyance and/or discomfort of any person. Continuous barking, yelping,
howling, and/or making other loud noises for 15 consecutive minutes by such
dog, whether confined inside a residence or building or to the outside area,
shall be deemed to have disturbed the peace and to have caused the annoyance
and discomfort of persons; provided, that at the time of the complaint, no
person or persons were trespassing or threatening to trespass upon the private
property of the owner, and provided that the dog was not being teased or
provoked in any manner.
   (B)   Any person who shall allow any dog habitually to remain or be lodged
or fed within any dwelling, building, yard, or enclosure owned or occupied by
such person shall be considered as harboring or keeping such dog.
   (C)   Upon an initial complaint, an enforcement officer shall warn the
person in writing of the violation. Upon a second such complaint within 30
days, the enforcement officer shall charge the person with a violation of this
section.
   (D)   Division (A) above does not apply to owners, operators, or employees
of licensed veterinary hospitals, licensed kennels, or licensed animal boarding
establishments, nor does this section apply to blind, deaf, or hearing
impaired, or mobility impaired persons when the dog serves as an assistance
dog.
   (E)   (1)   Whoever violates this section is guilty of a minor misdemeanor.
No owner, keeper, or harborer of a dog shall permit or allow such dog to annoy
or disturb one or more of the inhabitants of two or more separate residences of
the town by the frequent or habitual howling, yelping, barking, or making of
any other unreasonably loud and disturbing noises of such character, intensity,
and duration as to disturb the peace, quiet, and good order of the town.
      (2)   Any person who shall allow any animal habitually to remain or be
lodged or fed within any dwelling, building, yard, or enclosure owned or
occupied by such person shall be considered as keeping or harboring such
animal.
Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.006 HARBORING ROOSTERS AND CHICKENS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to own or harbor a rooster in the town limits.
   (B)   A resident of the town may not own or harbor more than two chickens
per lot, and not to exceed a total of six chickens per residence.
   (C)   If a person is in violation of this section, then he, she, or they may
be subject to the penalties under §
90.999.
(Ord. 2020-2, passed 9-3-2020) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.007 DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE.
   Any person or persons owning and/or harboring any dog or dogs shall keep a
muzzle on said dog or dogs to run at large.
(Ord. 113a, passed 5-14-1948)
CARE AND TREATMENT
§ 90.020 CARE AND TREATMENT OF ANIMALS.
   (A)   Every owner of an animal within the town shall see that his or her
animal:
      (1)   Is kept in a clean, sanitary, and healthy manner, is not confined
so as to be forced to stand, sit, or lie in its own excrement;
      (2)   Has proper and adequate food, water, shelter, and ventilation,
including quarters that are protected from excessive heat and cold and are of
sufficient size to permit the animal to exercise and move about. No animal
shall be tethered by use of a choke collar or on a leash less than 12 feet in
length, or of such unreasonable weight as to prevent the animal from moving
about freely;
      (3)   Is protected against abuse or mistreatment;
      (4)   Is diseased or injured, received proper care and, if diseased, is
segregated from other animals so as to prevent transmittal of the diseases; and
      (5)   Is maintained in compliance with all applicable federal, state, and
local laws and all regulations respecting animal care and control as are
adopted by the Department of Public Safety and in effect from time to time.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to beat, starve, or otherwise
mistreat any animal. Failure to comply with any requirement of division (A)
above shall be deemed mistreatment of the animal.
   (C)   Any person who violates any of the provisions of this section may be
given written notice of the practices or conditions which constitute the
violation and the enforcing authority may, where appropriate, suggest remedies.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.021 ABANDONMENT OF ANIMAL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to abandon any animal on any public or
private property.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.022 POISONING OF ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful to throw or deposit poisoned meat or any poison or
harmful substance in any street, alley, marketplace, or public place, or at any
private premises in the town, for the purpose of destroying any animal.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.023 ANIMAL FIGHTING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to incite or set any animal to fitting
within the town, and fights commonly known as “cockfights,” “bull fights,” and
“coon-on-a-log” shall be prohibited within the town.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
ANIMAL LICENSES
§ 90.035 WHEN REQUIRED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to own within the town any dog or
cat six months of age or older unless a current animal registration issued by
the town’s Police Department has been obtained for the dog or cat by that
person.
   (B)   There shall be no fees associated with the registration.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989; Ord. 2014-2, passed 5-1-2014) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.036 DISPLAY.
   A kennel or pet shop license pursuant to this subchapter shall at all times
be displayed prominently in the business office of the licensed kennel or pet
shop.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.037 REQUIREMENTS FOR KENNELS.
   In addition to obtaining the license required by this subchapter, all
kennels within the town limits shall:
   (A)   Be operated in such a manner as not to constitute a nuisance;
   (B)   Provide an isolation ward for boarded animals which are sick or
diseased sufficiently removed so as not to endanger the health of the other
animals;
   (C)   Retain the name, address, and telephone number of the owner and the
license number of each dog or cat boarded;
   (D)   Retain the name and address of each person selling, trading, or giving
any animal to the kennel;
   (E)   Keep all boarded animals caged or under the control of the owner
operator of the kennel; and
   (F)   With respect to all animals in the kennel, whether or not owned by the
kennel, comply with all requirements of §§
90.020 through
90.023.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.038 APPLICATION PROCESS.
   (A)   All applications for a kennel permit shall be completed on the
application form approved by the Town Council, and provided to the public by
the town’s Police Department.
   (B)   All completed applications shall be reviewed by the Town Marshal.
   (C)   Once the review of the application is concluded, the Town Marshal
shall approve or deny the applicant’s request. The Town Marshal shall make the
determination of approving or denying the application based on the following
factors:
      (1)   Prior complaints or calls made to the town’s Police Department
concerning animal control issues involving the property where the kennel is to
be located;
      (2)   Prior complaints or calls made to the town’s Police Department
concerning animal control issues involving the applicant or any member of the
applicant’s immediate household;
      (3)   Any convictions for animal cruelty, or any other offense relating
to animal health or welfare, that the applicant or any member of the
applicant’s immediate household may have; and
      (4)   Any other factor that the Town Marshal believes is relevant in
making the determination.
   (D)   If the Town Marshal approves the application for the kennel permit,
then the permit shall be issued as follows:
      (1)   Permit A: five to 16 dogs; and
      (2)   Permit B: more than 16 dogs.
   (E)   If the Town Marshal denies the application for the kennel permit, the
applicant shall be notified in writing, via certified mail, that his or her
application for the kennel permit has been denied, and in that written denial,
the applicant shall be notified of the proper procedures for requesting an
appeal of that determination.
(Ord. 2014-2, passed 5-1-2014)
§ 90.039 APPEAL PROCESS.
   (A)   If a person’s kennel permit is revoked, or an applicant is denied a
kennel permit, he or she may submit an appeal to the Town Clerk-Treasurer’s
office within 30 days from the date of the denial or revocation.
   (B)   All requests for appeals must be in writing and addressed to the
President of the Town Council, whereupon, the President of the Town Council
shall set the appeal for a hearing within 45 days of receipt of the written
request.
   (C)   The person requesting the hearing must notify, by certified mail,
return receipt requested, all landowners within a 250-foot radius of the
property where the kennel may be located. The notification must be on the form
supplied or approved by the town’s Police Department. The notice must have the
following information:
      (1)   Date, time, and place of hearing;
      (2)   Nature of the hearing; and
      (3)   The street address of the requested kennel permit.
   (D)   The notifications shall be completed and mailed to each neighboring
landowner ten days prior to the scheduled hearing date. The certified mail
return receipt cards must be filed with the Clerk’s office on or before the
date of the hearing. The hearing shall be held by the Town Council and the
ultimate approval or denial shall be made by the Town Council, within 30 days
from the date of the hearing. At the hearing, the person requesting the permit
or appealing the revocation of a permit may be heard along with anyone in
support of or in opposition to the appeal. The Town Council should conduct the
hearing in a manner consistent with its normal procedures.
(Ord. 2014-2, passed 5-1-2014)
RABIES CONTROL
§ 90.050 VACCINATION REQUIRED.
   Each dog and cat shall have a rabies vaccination more recent than one year.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.051 QUARANTINING AUTHORITY.
   For the purposes of this subchapter, the quarantining authority shall be the
Department of Public Safety and any agents or employees so designated, acting
pursuant to the directives and regulations of the Health and Hospital
Corporation of the county.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.052 SURRENDER OF ANIMAL BY OWNER.
   The owner of an animal which animal is suspected by the quarantining
authority of having bitten a person or been exposed to rabies, shall promptly
surrender the animal upon demand by said authority for purposes of quarantine
and observation, at the expense of the owner of the animal.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.053 FINDING OF RABIES AND GENERAL QUARANTINE.
   (A)   When a quarantined animal has been found rabid or if suspected of
being rabid by a licensed veterinarian and dies while under observation, the
quarantining authority shall take such action as is specified in such cases by
the State Board of Health and shall notify the proper public officials of
reports of human contacts made by and the diagnosis made of the animal.
   (B)   When a rabies report is made pursuant to division (A) above, the
quarantining authority shall recommend to the Department of Public Safety, a
quarantine within the town for a period of 30 days. Upon invocation of the
quarantine by the Department of Public Safety, any animal found at large within
the town may be destroyed without being impounded. During the quarantine
period, every animal bitten by an animal adjudged to be rabid shall be
confined, at its owner’s expense, or destroyed as specified by the State Board
of Health.
   (C)   During a rabies quarantine declared by the Department of Public
Safety, an owner or keeper of an animal resisting the quarantining authority
acting pursuant to this chapter or who permits an animal owned or kept by him
or her to be at large within shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed $100,
and impoundment of the animal suspected of rabies or of being in violation of
the rabies quarantine.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
ENFORCEMENT AND IMPOUNDMENT
§ 90.065 ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER POWERS.
   (A)   A person individually charged with the enforcement of this chapter
shall be designated “animal control officer.”
      (1)   Such officers shall have full power to enforce all provisions of
this chapter, including the right to proceed upon public and private property
within the town in pursuit of animals in violation of this chapter.
      (2)   (a)   Such officers shall not have the right to enter a privately
owned enclosure in pursuit of any animal without the consent of the owner,
lessee, or other occupant of the enclosure, or other legal process; provided,
however, if any animal is believed to be enclosed without adequate food or
water, or dead animals are believed to be enclosed, and such is not present and
cannot be located, and animal control officer may affix a notice to the
premises in an obvious location, directing the occupant to contact, the officer
at a given location and phone number.
         (b)   If contact is not made within 24 hours, however, the officer may
enter the premises to determine if this chapter has been violated.
   (B)   (1)   There is created the position of animal control officer to
assist in the enforcement of the provisions of this subchapter. The duties of
the animal control officer shall be to take and hold any dog, cat, or other
domestic animal found to be running uncontrolled.
      (2)   The animal control officer shall also have authority to seize and
impound all animals found to be dangerous animals, vicious animals at large,
stray abandoned public nuisance.
      (3)   The animal control officer shall provide the Town Marshal with a
weekly list of animals taken and the disposition of said animals.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989; Ord. 2024-1, passed 3-7-2024)
§ 90.066 INTERFERENCE WITH OFFICER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with an animal control
officer in the performance of his or her duties.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.067 GROUNDS FOR IMPOUNDMENT.
   Animals found at large in violation of this chapter shall be captured and
impounded. Any animal found confined or abandoned on private property in
violation of this chapter shall be impounded.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.068 NOTICE TO OWNER.
   Upon the impoundment of any animal, a reasonable attempt shall be made to
notify and inform the owner of the animal of the requirements of this article
for regaining the custody of the animal.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.069 RELEASE OF CAPTURED ANIMAL WITHOUT IMPOUNDMENT.
   When the owner of a captured animal is known, such animal need not be
impounded; but may be released to the owner upon payment of fees and fines, if
any, or upon the application for a license, if required.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
§ 90.070 IMPOUNDMENT FEES.
   Impoundment fees are as follows:
   (A)   First offense: $10;
   (B)   Second offense: $15; and
   (C)   Third and subsequent offenses: $20.
(Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989)
DANGEROUS ANIMALS
§ 90.085 KEEPING OF WILD, DANGEROUS ANIMALS; EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, maintain, or have in
possession or under control any wild animal, whether gratuitously or for a fee.
This section shall not be construed to apply to zoological parks, performing
animal exhibitions, or circuses, possessing valid permits as may be required
under state and/or federal law.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor or keep any wild animal
as a pet, unless a permit is granted by applicable state and federal
authorities, if required.
   (C)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      DANGEROUS ANIMAL. 
         (a)   Any animal which:
            1.   Has, off of its owner’s property, attacked another animal or
livestock;
            2.   Has attacked or which has attempted to attack, unprovoked, any
human being, whether on or off the owner’s property;
            3.   Has bitten any human being with said injury requiring stitches
and the loss or blood;
            4.   Has bitten or attacked a person, causing wound or injuries
creating a potential danger to the health or life of the victim;
            5.   Has a known propensity, tendency, or disposition to attack, to
cause injury or otherwise threaten or endanger the safety of humans or domestic
animals;
            6.   Has, according to the records of the appropriate authority,
killed or severely injured a domestic animal, with or without provocation,
while off the owners property; and/or
            7.   Any dog owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose
of dog fighting or any dog trained for fighting.
         (b)   However, no animal shall be considered a DANGEROUS ANIMAL if
injury or damage is inflicted by that animal upon a person or another animal if
such person or other animal, at the time of such injury or damage was
sustained, was committing a willful trespass upon the premises occupied by the
owner or keeper of the animal, or was teasing, tormenting, abusing, or
assaulting the animal or was committing or attempting to commit a crime.
         (c)   The definition excludes K-9 patrol dogs or police dogs used by
law enforcement agencies.
      DOMESTIC ANIMALS. Any animal that is a member of one of the following
species:
         (a)   Dog (canis familiaris);
         (b)   Cat (felis catus or felis domesticus);
         (c)   Cattle (bos domesticus or bos taurus of bos indicus);
         (d)   Horse (equus asinus);
         (e)   Donkey (equus aninus);
         (f)   Pig (sus scroffa);
         (g)   Sheep (ovis aries);
         (h)   Goat (capra hircus);
         (i)   Rabbit (oryctolagus cuniculus);
         (j)   Mouse (mus musculus);
         (k)   Rat (rattus rattus);
         (l)   Guinea pig (cavis proceelus);
         (m)   Hamster (mesocriecetus auratus);
         (n)   Chinchilla (chinchilla langier);
         (o)   Gerbil (gerbillus gerbillus);
         (p)   Mink;
         (q)   Cow or ox (bovine); or
         (r)   Ferret.
      EXOTIC ANIMAL. Any animal whose normal native habitat is not indigenous
to the continental United States, excluding Alaska and Hawaii, except fish and
furbearing animals commercially bred for the furrier trade and birds defined
under federal regulations, and nonpoisonous snakes and reptiles.
      PUBLIC NUISANCE. Any animal or animals which:
         (a)   Molests or disturbs persons or vehicles by chasing, barking, or
biting;
         (b)   Attacks other animal(s) or person(s);
         (c)   Is at large;
         (d)   Damages private or public property;
         (e)   Causes frequent or long continued noises or other sounds common
to its species which disturbs the comfort or repose of any person in the
immediate neighborhood;
         (f)   Causes foul or noxious odors which offend residents in the
neighborhood;
         (g)   Trespasses on the private property of persons other than the
owner of the animal;
         (h)   Runs uncontrolled;
         (i)   Defecates upon any public place or upon premises not owned or
controlled by the owner or harborer unless promptly removed by the animal owner
or harborer; and
         (j)   Creates an insect breeding and/or attraction site through to an
accumulation of excreta.
   VICIOUS ANIMAL. Any animals that has, without provocations, attacked a human
being or other animal, or an animal that by its behavior or physical condition
constitutes an immediate and serious physical or health threat to human beings
or animals, or any animal which has previously attacked or bitten any human
being or other animal or two or more reported occasions, or any potentially
dangerous dog. VICIOUS ANIMAL shall also include an animal that has attacked
and killed another domestic animal, with or without provocation, while off the
owner’s property.
   WILD ANIMAL. Any animal not a domestic or exotic animal, with the exception
of small, nonpoisonous aquatic or amphibious animals and small cage birds,
which are normally found in a wild state.
(Ord. 2024-1, passed 3-7-2024) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.086 DETERMINATION OF DANGEROUS ANIMALS.
   (A)   The Town Marshal or his or her designee shall, upon receipt of
reliable information, make a determination that an animal is a dangerous
animal. Notice of said determination shall be personally delivered or shall be
sent by certified letter to the owner or harborer. The owner or harborer of
said animal may, within five days or receipt of said notice, request a
detention hearing by requesting the same, by written request, to the Town
Marshal within five days of said notice. If said owner or harborer does not
make such written request within five days as set forth herein, said animal
shall be deemed a dangerous animal as defined in this subchapter. If requested
in a timely manner, a determination shall be conducted in the following manner.
      (1)   A determinations hearing shall be conducted by the Town Council
whenever there is cause to believe that a dog may be a dangerous animal, as
defined herein. Said hearing shall be conducted within five days of serving
notice to the owner or harborer.
      (2)   Pending the outcome of such a hearing, the dog must be securely
confined in a humane manner either on the premises of the owner of harborer,
with a licensed veterinarian or confined by the town.
      (3)   The Marshal and the Town Council shall determine whether to declare
the animal be a dangerous animal based upon the evidence and testimony
presented at the time of the hearing by the owner, witnesses to any incident(s)
which may be considered germane to such a determination, Health Department
personnel, animal control personnel, police, or any other person possessing
information pertinent to such determination.
      (4)   The Marshal shall issued written finding within five days after the
determination hearing. The owner of possessor of the animal found to be
dangerous by this hearing has the right to appeal the decision within three
days of receiving such decision to the town.
   (B)   The owner or harborer of a dangerous animal shall restrain the animal
in the following manner.
      (1)   While on the owner’s or harborer’s property, a dangerous animal
must be securely enclosed and the locked pen or structure must have minimum
dimensions of five feet by ten feet and must have secure sides and a secure
top. If it has no bottom secured to the sides, the sides must be embedded into
the ground no less than two feet. The enclosure must also provide protection
from the elements for the animal.
      (2)   A dangerous animal may be off the owner’s premises it is muzzled
and restrained by a substantial chain or leash not exceeding six feet in length
and under control of a responsible person. The muzzle must be made in a manner
that will not cause injury to the animal or interfere with its vision or
respiration but must prevent it from biting any person or animal.
(Ord. 2024-1, passed 3-7-2024)
§ 90.087 REGULATIONS GOVERNING DANGEROUS ANIMALS.
   (A)   Sign requirements. The owner or harborer of a dangerous animal shall
display a sign on his or her premises warning that there is a dangerous animal
on the property. This sign shall be visible and capable of being read from the
public highway or thoroughfare. In addition, the owner shall conspicuously
display a sign warning children of the presence of a dangerous animal.
   (B)   Liability insurance requirements. The owner or harborer of a dangerous
animal shall present to the Marshal proof that the owner or harborer has
procured liability insurance in the amount of a least $100,000 covering the 12-
month period during which licensing is sought. This policy shall contain a
provision requiring the town to be named as an additional insured for the sole
purposes of the town to be notified by the insurance company of any
cancellation, termination, or expiration of the policy.
   (C)   Liability of parents or guardians of minor children. The parents or
guardians of any minor child who is the owner or harborer of any animal shall
be responsible for compliance with this subchapter regarding said animal and
shall be subject to all penalties for violations of this subchapter which
result from the actions or reactions of the minor child and/or the conduct and
control of the animal, and shall be further liable for all injuries and
property damage sustained by any person or domestic animal caused by an
unprovoked attack by the animal.
   (D)   Inspection. No owner of harborer of an animal may refuse access to
their premises to any police officer, or animal control officer, of the stated
purpose of said inspection or investigation is to investigate compliance with
or alleged violations of the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2024-1, passed 3-7-2024) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   The owner or keeper of an animal determined to be at large in
violation of §
90.002 shall be punishable with respect to each such animal by fines, as
follows:
      (1)   First offense: $12.50;
      (2)   Second offense: $25;
      (3)   Third offense: $50; and
      (4)   Subsequent offenses: $20 times the number of offenses committed by
the person, including the first three times.
   (C)   (1)   Any person found guilty to permitting a nuisance to exist, as
defined by §
90.002, shall be fined:
         (a)   First offense: not less than $25 nor more than $50;
         (b)   Second offense: not less than $50 nor more than $75;
         (c)   Third offense: not less than $75 nor more than $100; and
         (d)   Fourth offense: not less than $100 nor more than $150.
      (2)   The second, third, and fourth offenses will be subject to happening
within a consecutive 12-month time period.
   (D)   Any persons who violates §
90.004 shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $25. Upon subsequent
violation by that person, the court shall, upon request, order the animal
forfeited and/or destroyed.
   (E)   Any person or persons that violates §
90.007 shall, on conviction therefore, be fined in any sum not less that $10
and not more than $50.
   (F)   (1)   Any violation of §
90.020 shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $25.
      (2)   Any person convicted of a second or subsequent offense of violating
the provisions of §
90.020 shall be fined in an amount not less than $50 and the court, upon
request, shall order a forfeiture or other disposition of the animal involved.
Any judgment which calls for a fine or forfeiture or other disposition of the
animal by the town or any third party shall include the collection costs, and
the like as part of the judgment.
   (G)   A violation of §
90.021 shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $50.
   (H)   The owner of a dog or cat which does not have a rabies vaccination
more recent than one year shall be punishable by a fine in the following
amounts, plus the expense to the quarantining authority of procuring for the
animal a current rabies vaccination:
      (1)   First offense: $10;
      (2)   Second offense: $25;
      (3)   Third offense: $50; and
      (4)   Subsequent offenses: $50 times the number of offenses, including
the first three offenses.
   (I)   Any violation of §
90.066 shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $50.
   (J)   (1)   Any person found in violation to permitting a public nuisance or
animal nuisance to exist as defined by §
90.087 shall be fined:
         (a)   Not less than $15 nor more than $100 for the first offense;
         (b)   Not less than $40 nor more than $500 for the second offense
within a consecutive 12-month period;
         (c)   Not less than $100 nor more than $500 for the third offense
within a consecutive 12-month period; and
         (d)   Not less than $200 not more than $500 for the fourth offense
within a consecutive 12-month period.
      (2)   Any person found guilty of violating any provision of §§
90.065 and
90.086, shall be fined not less than $10 nor more than $500 for each offense.
      (3)   Any person found in violation of any provision of §
90.087 shall be fined not less than $200 and not more than $500 for each
offense. The court may further order the owner or harborer of a dangerous
animal to permanently remove said animal from the town.
      (4)   In addition to the foregoing fines, the owner or harborer of any
animal impounded, held or disposed of by the town through enforcement of §§
90.085 to 90.087 shall pay the additional sum of $25.
(Ord. 113a, passed 5-14-1948; Ord. 1989-2, passed 5-9-1989; Ord. 2000-13,
passed - -; Ord. 2024-1, passed 3-7-2024)
CHAPTER 91: HEALTH AND SANITATION; NUISANCES

91.21   Leaving abandoned or inoperative vehicles on public property

91.24   Impounding

NUISANCES
§ 91.01 NUISANCE PROPERTIES.
   No person owning, leasing, occupying, or having charge of any premises shall
maintain or keep any nuisance thereon, nor shall any such person keep or
maintain such premises in a manner causing substantial diminution in the value
of the other property in the neighborhood in which such premises are located.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.02 DEFINITION.
   (A)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the term NUISANCE is defined to
mean any condition of building exteriors or premises which is detrimental to
the property of others or which causes or tends to cause substantial diminution
in the value of other property in the neighborhood in which the premises are
located, or the maintenance of an unsafe dwelling or building within the town.
   (B)   In addition thereto, the term NUISANCE shall also include:
      (1)   The accumulation of, outside of dwellings or other buildings on
residential property: junk, trash, or debris, including but no limited to,
garbage, discarded and refuse materials, waste materials, leaves, iron, tin,
furniture, appliances, cans, and paper;
      (2)   The storage of any motor vehicle parts, tires, building materials
or any other supplies or materials; other than in an enclosed building or
within an area adequately concealed so as not to be visible from any
surrounding residential or public properties;
      (3)   The existence of thistles, burdock, jimson weeds, ragweeds,
milkweeds, poison ivy, poison oak, ironweeds, and all other noxious weeds rank
vegetation and grass in excess of a height of six inches. Undeveloped lots
located within the town limits, that are over one acre in size may be used for
agriculture planting only; and
      (4)   The failure to keep an animal’s pen, yard, lot, or other enclosure
in a sanitary condition and flee from preventable offensive odors.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2001-7, passed 7-5-2001; Ord. 2007-4,
passed 6-7-2007; Ord. 2017-1, passed 1-5-2017)
§ 91.03 UNSAFE PREMISES.
   For purposes of this subchapter, an UNSAFE PREMISES is any dwelling or
building that is:
   (A)   In an impaired structural condition that makes it unsafe to a person
or property;
   (B)   A fire hazard;
   (C)   A hazard to public health; and/or
   (D)   Has parts thereof which are so attached that they may fail or injure
persons or property.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000)
§ 91.04 REMEDY OF NUISANCES.
   (A)   Any person violating the provisions of this subchapter may be ordered
to remedy and cure the conditions which constitute the nuisance. Such order
shall be made by the President of the Town Council or the Town Marshal or Chief
of Police of the town, or their designee. The order shall contain:
      (1)   The name of the owner or other person to whom the order is
directed;
      (2)   The legal description or address of the premises that the subject
of the order;
      (3)   The action the order requires; and
      (4)   The period of time in which the action is required to be
accomplished, measured from the time the action is required to be accomplished,
measured from the time of which the notice is given.
   (B)   The order shall be delivered personally or by certified mail to the
owner or other person to whom the order is directed.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.05 ABATEMENT PROCEDURE.
   (A)   On the failure, neglect, or refusal of any owner or such agent so
notified, to abate said nuisance located on such property or on the sidewalk
abutting these areas within five days after receiving the written notice
provided for in §
91.04, or within 14 days after the date of such notice in the event the same is
returned by the Post Office Department because of its inability to make
delivery or the failure of the owner to accept the notice provided the notice
was properly addressed to the last known address of such owner or agent as
shown on the tax records of the county, the town’s Police Department or anyone
appointed by the town’s Police Department.
   (B)   When the town has effected the removal of such nuisance, and has not
been paid the actual costs thereof, such costs shall be charged to the owner of
such property on the next regular tax bill forwarded to such owner by the
county. This charge shall be due and payable by the owner at the time of
payment of the tax bill.
   (C)   If the landowner fails to remove the nuisance within the time
prescribed, the town may remove the nuisance. The Clerk-Treasurer must make a
certified statement of the actual cost incurred by the town in the removal. The
statement must be delivered to the owner of the property by a law enforcement
officer of the town or by certified mail, return receipt requested, and the
owner shall pay the amount to the Clerk-Treasurer. If the landowner fails to
pay the amount within ten days after receiving the statement, a certified copy
of the statement of costs shall be filed in the Office of the Auditor of the
county. The Auditor shall place the amount claimed on the tax duplicate against
the property affected by the work, and the amount shall be collected as taxes
are collected and shall be disbursed to the General Fund of the town.
   (D)   In lieu of filing of a lien as set out in divisions (B) and (C) above,
the town may seek and be granted, in any court of competent jurisdiction,
injunctive relief to enforce this subchapter. Any action brought pursuant to
this section shall prohibit a lien being filed as set out herein for the same
acts alleged in the complaint by the town pursuant to this section.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2001-7, passed 7-5-2001; Ord. 2007-4,
passed 6-7-2007) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.06 PROVISIONS NOT EXCLUSIVE.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not be construed to be the exclusive
means of dealing with the regulation and control of housing and sanitation and
with nuisances, but shall be a remedy provided in addition to the applicable
state statutes and other applicable laws.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000)
§ 91.07 LIEN; NOTICE PROCEDURE.
   Failure to comply with the judgment entered in this clause will result in a
lien filed on the tax duplicated against the property described herein. Written
notice of such action will be given to the property owner by certified mail.
(Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000)
ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES
§ 91.20 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED VEHICLE.
      (1)   Any vehicle which is left on private property for more than 48
hours without the permission of the person having the right to the possession
of the property.
      (2)   Any vehicle which is left on public property for 48 hours or longer
without permission of the Town Marshal or his or her designee.
   INOPERATIVE MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle not moved for 60 consecutive
days shall be presumed INOPERATIVE.
   JUNK MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle meeting any three of the following
criteria:
      (1)   Three years old or older;
      (2)   Disabling damage, such damage including, but not limited to, any of
the following:
         (a)   Missing wheel;
         (b)   Missing or deflated tire;
         (c)   Missing motor; and/or
         (d)   Missing transmission.
      (3)   Fair market value less than $400;
      (4)   Inoperative; and/or
      (5)   Unlicensed or improperly licensed.
   PERSON. Includes any private person or corporate entity.
   PROPERTY. Any real property within the municipality which is not a street,
alley, or highway.
   VEHICLE. Includes any device in, upon or by which a person or property is or
may be transported or drawn upon any roadway.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2017-4, passed 6-1-2017)
§ 91.21 LEAVING ABANDONED OR INOPERATIVE VEHICLES ON PUBLIC PROPERTY.
    No person shall leave or abandon any partially dismantled or otherwise
inoperative motor vehicle on any public street, alley, highway, or any other
public property within the municipality.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2017-4, passed 6-1-2017) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.22 ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   No person shall willfully leave a discarded, inoperative, or abandoned
vehicle on private property without the permission of the person having the
right to the possession of the property. For purposes of this section, the fact
that a vehicle has been left on private property without the permission or
notification of the person having the right of possession of this property is
prima facie evidence of abandonment.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2017-4, passed 6-1-2017) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.23 KEEPING INOPERATIVE, JUNK, OR ABANDONED VEHICLES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   No person in charge or in control of any real property within the
municipality, whether as an owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise shall
allow any inoperative, junk, or abandoned vehicle to remain on the property
within their control longer than seven days after the receipt of a written
notice from the Town Marshal or any other member of the Town Marshal’s
Department designated by the Town Marshal instruction that person to remove
this inoperative, junk, or abandoned vehicle from the property. This section
shall not apply to a vehicle stored in an enclosed building or to commercial
garages, repair shops, used car dealers, or junk yards operated in a lawful
manner.
   (B)   Notice required under division (A) above shall be deemed to be
adequate if the Town Marshal or his or her designee, causes that notice to be
affixed to the vehicle or upon the door of any residence located on the
property where the vehicle is found and delivering the notice in person, by
certified mail, or by leaving the notice affixed to the door and mailing a copy
of the same to the registered owner, the owner of the real estate or the
tenant, occupant, or lessee of the private property upon which this
inoperative, junk, or abandoned vehicle is found.
   (C)   The notice required under division (A) above should state the
following:
      (1)   The date and time of the notice;
      (2)   A description of the inoperative, junk, or abandoned vehicle;
      (3)   The license plate number on the vehicle, if any;
      (4)   The identity of the owner or person in charge of the real property
upon which the vehicle is located;
      (5)   That the person responsible for this vehicle has seven days after
the date and time noted above in the order to remove this vehicle because it is
alleged that the vehicle is a inoperative, junk, or abandoned vehicle as
defined in §
91.20;
      (6)   A copy of the ordinance should be attached; and
      (7)   A statement indicating that if the vehicle is not removed from the
property within seven days of the date and time affixed above, this would be
prima facie evidence of the fact that it is a inoperative, junk, or abandoned
vehicle in violation of this section and, thus, the person to whom the notice
is directed could be subject to penalties provided by this subchapter.
   (D)   If the person whom the notice is directed contents that the vehicle is
operable and not junk or abandoned, he or she or a designee should take it to
the Police Department of the town for inspection in compliance with the
inspection laws of the state. If this is done within seven days of the time of
the giving of the notice, this shall be deemed to be prima facie evidence that
the vehicle in question is not junk, abandoned, or inoperative.
   (E)   For purposes of this section, if the seven days granted ends after 5:
00 p.m. Friday and before 12:00 p.m. on the following Monday, the time shall be
extended to 5:00 p.m. that Monday. If it ends on a legal holiday, the time
shall be extended 24 hours following the conclusion of the legal holiday.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2017-4, passed 6-1-2017) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.24 IMPOUNDING.
   (A)   The Town Marshal or his or her designee may impound any vehicle found
in violation of this subchapter. This vehicle shall remain impounded until
lawfully claimed or disposed of in accordance with I.C. 9-22-1-5 et seq.
   (B)   The Town Marshal or his or her designee may also impound a vehicle
that is inoperative, junk, or that has been abandoned, upon complaint of an
owner of a repair garage or place of storage for a vehicle for a vehicle when
the vehicle has been left for longer than that agreed upon by the owner of the
repair garage or place of storage, his or her agent or employee and the owner
or operator of the vehicle. Before taking possession of the vehicle, the Town
Marshal or his or her designee shall give a seven-day notice to the owner of
the vehicle of his or her intention to impound this vehicle at the end of the
seven days if it is not lawfully removed from the repair garage or other place
of storage.
   (C)   The Town Marshal shall designate a place of storage for vehicles
impounded under this section.
   (D)   The owner of a vehicle impounded under this section may reclaim it
upon payment of any expenses or charges incurred in its removal and storage,
and presentation of proof of ownership, which may be evidenced by a certificate
of title to the vehicle.
   (E)   If the vehicle remains unclaimed by the owner for a period of 30 days,
this vehicle may be disposed of in accordance with the procedures established
by I.C. 9-22-1-13 et seq.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2017-4, passed 6-1-2017) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person who is in violation of §§
91.01 to
91.07, who has been served with an order directed to them pursuant to §
91.04, and who fails to take the required action within the time period
specified in the order, shall be guilty of a Class B infraction.
   (C)   Any person, firm, or corporation who shall violate any of the
provisions of §§
91.20 to
91.24 shall, upon conviction, be fined in any sum not exceeding $500.
(Ord. 1994-1, passed 3-24-1994; Ord. 2000-2, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2017-4,
passed 6-1-2017)
CHAPTER 92: TREES
Section
   
92.01   Definitions
   
92.02   Street tree species
   
92.03   Distance from street corners and fireplugs
   
92.04   Utilities
   
92.05   Public tree care
   
92.06   Tree topping
   
92.07   Pruning, corner clearance
   
92.08   Dead or diseased tree removal on private property
   
92.09   Removal of stumps
 
   
92.99   Penalty
§ 92.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PARK TREES. Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation in public
parks having individual names, and all areas owned by the town, or to which the
public has free access as a park.
   STREET TREES. Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation on land
lying between property lines on either side of all streets, avenues, or ways
within the town.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017)
§ 92.02 STREET TREE SPECIES.
   (A)   The following trees shall not be used for street tree planting in the
public right-of-way:
      (1)   Carolina Poplar;
      (2)   Cottonwood;
      (3)   Lonbardy Poplar;
      (4)   Box Elder;
      (5)   Maple (all types);
      (6)   Ailanthus or Tree of Heaven;
      (7)   Chinese Elm;
      (8)   Siberian Elm;
      (9)   Willows; and
      (10)   Catalpas.
   (B)   (1)   The species listed below are approved for street tree planting
on the public right-of-way between the sidewalk and the curb:
         (a)   Serviceberry;
         (b)   Lilac Tree;
         (c)   Locust;
         (d)   Elm; and
         (e)   Zelkova.
      (2)   Any other trees must be approved in writing by the Town Council.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.03 DISTANCE FROM STREET CORNERS AND FIREPLUGS.
   No street tree shall be planted closer than 35 feet of any street corner,
measured from the point of nearest intersecting curbs or curblines. No street
tree shall be planted closer than ten feet of any fireplug.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.04 UTILITIES.
   No street trees other than those species listed as small trees in §
92.02(B)(1) may be planted under or within ten lateral feet of any overhead
utility wire, or over or within five lateral feet of any underground water
line, sewer line, transmission line, or other utility.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.05 PUBLIC TREE CARE.
   (A)   The town shall have the right to plant, prune, maintain, and remove
trees, plants, and shrubs within the lines of all streets, alleys, avenues,
lanes, squares, and public grounds, as may be necessary to insure public safety
or the preserve or enhance the symmetry and beauty of such public grounds.
   (B)   The Town Council may remove or cause or order to be removed, any tree
or part thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which by reason of its
nature is injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines, or
other public improvements, or is affected with any injurious fungus, insect, or
other pest. This section does not prohibit the planting of street trees by
adjacent property owners providing that the selection of said trees is in
accordance with §§
92.02 through
92.04.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.06 TREE TOPPING.
   It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any person, firm, or town
department to top any street tree, park tree, or other tree on public property.
TOPPING is defined as the severe cutting back of limbs to stubs larger than
three inches in diameter within the tree’s crown to such a degree so as to
removed the normal canopy and disfigure the tree. Trees severely damaged by
storms or other causes, or certain trees under utility wires or other
obstructions where other pruning practices are impractical may be exempted from
this chapter at the determination of the Town Council.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.07 PRUNING, CORNER CLEARANCE.
   Every owner of any tree overhanging any street or right-of-way within the
town shall prune the branches so that such branches shall not obstruct the
light from any street lamp or obstruct the view of any street or sidewalk. Said
owners shall remove all dead, diseased, or dangerous trees, or broken or
decayed limbs, which constitute a menace to the safety of the public. The town
shall have the right to prune any tree or shrub on private property when it
interferes with the proper spread of light along the street from a streetlight
or interferes with visibility of any traffic control device or sign.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.08 DEAD OR DISEASED TREE REMOVAL ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   The town shall have the right to cause the removal of any dead or diseased
trees on private property within the town, when such trees constitute a hazard
to life and property, or harbor insects or disease which constitute a potential
threat to other trees within the town. The Town Council will notify in writing
the owners of such trees. Said owners, at their own expense, shall do removal
within 60 days after the date of service of notice. In the event of failure of
the owners to comply with such provisions, the town shall have the authority to
remove such trees and charge the cost of removal on the owner’s property tax
notice.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017)
§ 92.09 REMOVAL OF STUMPS.
   All stumps of street and park trees shall be removed below the surface of
the ground so that the top of the stump shall not project above the surface of
the ground.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be, upon conviction
or plea of guilty, subject to a fine not to exceed $2,500, and as further
stated in §
10.99.
(Ord. 2004-6, passed 6-3-2004; Ord. 2017-9, passed 12-7-2017)
CHAPTER 93: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
Section
Sidewalk Repair and Construction
   
93.01   Unsafe sidewalk defined
   
93.02   Sidewalk repair and construction
   
93.03   Owner’s liability to town

Display of Address
   
93.15   Requirement
   
93.16   Display of street number and address
