§ 150.01 TITLE.
   This chapter, and all ordinances supplemental or amendatory hereto, shall be
known as the “Building Code of the Town of Parker City, Indiana,” may be cited
as such, and will be referred to herein as “this chapter.”
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.02 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to provide minimum standards for the
protection of life, limb, health, environment, public safety, and welfare, and
for the conservation of energy in the design and construction of buildings and
structures.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.03 SCOPE.
   The provisions of this chapter apply to the construction, alteration,
repair, use, occupancy, and maintenance and additions to all buildings and
structures, other than fences, in the town.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.04 AUTHORITY.
   The Building Commissioner of the county, hereinafter referred to as the
Building Commissioner, after having been designated as the officer of a single
agency to administer and enforce this chapter, is authorized in the name of the
town, to issue building permits, collect permit fees, perform inspections,
order correction of violations of this chapter, and authorize occupancy of
buildings and structures within the corporate limits of the town.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.05 ENTRY.
   Upon presentation of proper credentials, the Building Commissioner or his or
her duly authorized representatives may enter at reasonable times any building,
structure, or premises in the town to perform any duty imposed upon him or her
by this chapter.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.06 VIOLATIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation, whether as owner,
lessee, sub-lessee, or occupant, to erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair,
improve, remove, convert, demolish, equip, use, occupy, or maintain any
building or structure, other than fences, in the town, or cause or permit the
same to be done, contrary to or in violation of the provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.07 RIGHT OF APPEAL.
   Any person, partnership, association, or corporation aggrieved by a decision
of the regulating agency shall have the right of appeal as in other civil
actions provided that a 15-day written notice of their intention to do so is
given to the Board of County Commissioners by registered mail. The notice shall
concisely state their grievance.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.08 ADOPTION OF REGULATIONS BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   The following rules, regulations, and codes are adopted by reference
as the rules and regulations governing the construction and alteration of
buildings and structures in the town:
      (1)   Construction Rules and Regulations, Volume I, 1980 Edition of the
State of Indiana (660 I.A.C. 1-1.1) originally published as (3 I.R. 2148) which
identifies, amends and incorporates therein the Uniform Building Code, 1979
Edition, and the Uniform Building Code Standards, 1979 Edition;
      (2)   Indiana Electrical Rules, 1981 Edition (675 I.A.C. 17-1.8)
originally published as (4 I.R. 798) which identifies, amends and incorporates
therein the National Electrical Code, 1981 Edition;
      (3)   Indiana Plumbing Rules, 1981 Edition, (675 I.A.C. 16-1.4)
originally published as (4 I.R. 2398) which identifies, amends and incorporates
therein the Uniform Plumbing Code, 1979 Edition;
      (4)   Indiana Mechanical Rules, 1981 Edition, (675 I.A.C. 18-1.6)
originally published as (4 I.R. 1828) which identifies, amends, and
incorporates therein the Uniform Mechanical Code, 1979 Edition;
      (5)   One and Two Family Dwelling Code of Indiana, (675 I.A.C. 14-4.4)
originally published as (4 I.R. 916) which identifies, amends and incorporates
therein the One and Two Family Dwelling Code, 1979 Edition;
      (6)   Indiana Energy Conservation Rules and Regulations for New Building
Construction, Volume V, 1979 Edition. (675 I.A.C. 19-4) (1980 Supp.) published
under that title; and
      (7)   Swimming Pool Code (675 I.A.C. 20-1.1) (1979 Supp.) published as
the Indiana Swimming Pool Code, 1978 Edition.
   (B)   Two copies of this chapter and rules, regulations, and codes adopted
herein by reference are on file as required by law in the Office of the
Building Commissioner of the county.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981; Ord. 143, passed 12-29-1981)
§ 150.09 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   A permit shall be obtained before beginning construction, alteration, or
repair of any building or structure, the cost of which exceeds $500 for
electrical, plumbing, heating, air conditioning, or combination, and $1,500 for
building structure, foundation, mechanical, or combination for said
improvements, using forms furnished by the Building Commissioner. All permits
shall be issued by the Building Commissioner, and all fees provided for herein
shall be paid to the county.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.10 PLANS.
   No permits shall be issued for the foregoing purposes, unless the
application for such permit is accompanied by a plat or sketch of the proposed
location showing lot boundaries, and by plans and specifications showing all
work to be done. All plans for building construction under the authority of the
Administrative Building Council of the state must also be filed with the
Administrative Building Council who will issue an approved certificate of
compliance, under the provisions of I.C. 22-11-1-12. In all such cases under
the authority of said Administrative Building Council, no local permits shall
be issued hereunder until a copy of the release for construction from the
Administrative Building Council is received by the Building Commissioner.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.11 COMPLIANCE.
   All work done under any permit issued hereunder shall be in full compliance
with all other ordinances pertaining thereto, and in addition to the fees for
permits hereinafter provided for, there shall be paid the fees prescribed in
such ordinances.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.12 FEES.
The fee for all permits shall be as follows:
   (A)   For work costing more than $500 to $2,000: $10;
   (B)   For work costing more than $2,000 to $6,000: $15;
   (C)   For work costing more than $6,000 to $10,000: $20;
   (D)   For work costing more than $10,000 and less than $100,000, the fee
shall be $2.50 for each 1,000 of cost or part thereof; and
   (E)   For all work costing $100,000 or more, the fee shall be $250 plus
$0.02 per square foot.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981; Ord. 140, passed 5-20-1981)
§ 150.13 REVIEW OF APPLICATION.
   Prior to the issuance of any building permit hereunder, the Building
Commissioner shall:
   (A)   Review all building permit applications to determine full compliance
with the provisions of this chapter;
   (B)   Review all building permit applications for new construction or
substantial improvements to determine whether proposed building sites will be
reasonably safe from flooding;
   (C)   Review building permit applications for major repairs within the flood
plain area having special flood hazards to determine that the proposed repair:
      (1)   Uses construction materials and utility equipment that are
resistant to flood damage; and
      (2)   Uses construction methods and practices that will minimize flood
damage.
   (D)   Review building permit applications for new construction or
substantial improvements within the flood plain area having special flood
hazards to assure that the proposed construction (including prefabricated and
mobile homes):
      (1)   Is protected against flood damage;
      (2)   Is designed (or modified) and anchored to prevent flotation,
collapse, or lateral movement of the structure;
      (3)   Uses construction materials and utility equipment that are
resistant to flood damage; and
      (4)   Uses construction methods and practices that will minimize flood
damage.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.14 INSPECTIONS.
   After the issuance of any building permit hereunder, the Building
Commissioner shall make such inspections of the work being done under such
permit as are necessary to ensure full compliance with the provisions of this
chapter and the terms of the permit.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.15 STOP ORDER.
   Whenever any work is being done contrary to the provisions of this chapter,
the Building Commissioner may order the work stopped by notice in writing
served on any persons engaged in the doing or causing such work to be done, and
any such persons shall forthwith stop such work until authorized by the
Building Commissioner to proceed with the work.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.16 INTERPRETATION.
   Whenever in the building regulations it is provided that anything must be
done to the approval of or subject to the direction of the Building
Commissioner or any other officer of the Commission, this shall be construed to
give such officer only the discretion of determining whether the rules and
standards established by ordinance have been complied with; and no such
provision shall be construed as giving any officer discretionary powers as to
what such regulations, codes, or standards shall be, or power to require
conditions not prescribed by ordinances or to enforce ordinance provisions in
an arbitrary or discriminating manner.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.17 CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY.
   No certificate of occupancy for any building or structure erected, altered,
or repaired after the adoption of this chapter shall be issued unless such
building or structure was erected, altered, or repaired in compliance with the
provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.18 STANDARDS.
   All work on the construction, alteration, and repair of buildings and other
structures shall be performed in a good and workmanlike manner according to
accepted standards and practices in the trade.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.19 REMEDIES.
   The Building Commissioner shall, in the name of the town, bring actions in
the Circuit or County Courts of the county for mandatory and injunctive relief
in the enforcement of and to secure compliance with any order or orders made by
the Building Commissioner, and any such action for mandatory or injunctive
relief may be joined with an action to recover the penalties provided for in
this chapter.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
§ 150.20 COUNTY TO ENFORCE.
   (A)   The county is the single agency designated to administer building
regulations and inspection within the boundaries of the units of government
which are parties hereto.
   (B)   The Building Commissioner of the county is authorized and empowered to
issue building permits, make inspections, order correction of violations, issue
certificates of occupancy, and to perform such other ministerial duties as are
commonly performed in the execution of his or her office, on behalf of the
parties hereto.
(Res. passed - -)
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   If any person, firm, or corporation shall violate any of the provisions of
this chapter, or shall do any act prohibited herein, or shall fail to perform
any duty lawfully enjoined, within the time prescribed by the Building
Commissioner, in connection with the provisions of this chapter, for each such
violation; failure or refusal, such person, firm, or corporation, shall
constitute a Class C infraction. Each day such violation continues shall be a
separate offense.
(Ord. 138, passed 2-18-1981)
CHAPTER 151: UNSAFE BUILDINGS
Section
   
151.01   Enforcement authority
   
151.02   Hearing authority
   
151.03   Powers and duties
   
151.04   Performance of work and costs thereof
   
151.05   Liability for costs
§ 151.01 ENFORCEMENT AUTHORITY.
   It shall be the duty of the police officers of the town to enforce the
provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2000-3, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2006-5, passed 10-5-2006; Ord. 2024-2,
passed 3-7-2024)
§ 151.02 HEARING AUTHORITY.
   It shall be the duty of the Town Council to act as the hearing authority for
all matters requiring a hearing under this chapter.
(Ord. 2000-3, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2006-5, passed 10-5-2006; Ord. 2024-2,
passed 3-7-2024)
§ 151.03 POWERS AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The Enforcement Authority may issue an order requiring action relative
to any vacant premises deemed unsafe; sealing against intrusion by unauthorized
persons; extermination of vermin in and about the premises, removal of trash,
debris, or fire hazardous material in and about the unsafe premises; repair or
rehabilitation to bring the building into compliance with any ordinance, code,
or statute or for human habitation, occupancy, or use; removal of part of a
building; and removal of a building.
   (B)   For any action other than that described in this section, a hearing
shall be held pursuant to I.C. 36-7-9-7.
   (C)   An order issued by the Enforcement Authority will contain the
following information:
      (1)   The name of the person to whom the order is issued (which person
shall be a person having a substantial property interest in the premises, the
definition of which is found in I.C. 36-7-9 and which is incorporated by
reference;
      (2)   The legal description or address of the unsafe premises that arc
the subject of the order;
      (3)   The action that the order requires;
      (4)   The period of time in which the action is required to be
accomplished (which is to be measured from the date the notice is given);
      (5)   If a hearing is required, a statement indicating the exact time and
place of the hearing and stating that the person to whom the order was issued
is entitled to appear with or without legal counsel, present evidence, cross-
examine opposing witnesses, and present argument;
      (6)   If a hearing is not required, a statement that the order becomes
final ten days after notice is given, unless a hearing is requested in writing
by a person with a “substantial property interest;”
      (7)   The following statement: A person who has been issued and has
received notice of an order relative to unsafe and abandoned premises and has
not complied with said order:
         (a)   Must supply fill information regarding the order to a person who
takes or agrees to take a substantial interest in the premises before
transferring or agreeing to transfer that interest; and
         (b)   Must, within five days after transferring or agreeing to
transfer a substantial property interest in the premises, supply the town with
written copies of the fill name, address, and telephone number of the person
taking a substantial property interest in the premises and the legal instrument
under which the transfer or agreement to transfer the interest is accomplished.
         (c)   If a judgment is obtained against the town or other governmental
entity for the failure to provide notice of its actions, a person who failed to
comply with obligation is liable to the town of the amount of the judgment.
      (8)   The name, address, and telephone number of the Enforcement
Authority.
   (D)   The order must allow at least ten days from the time when notice of
the order is given to accomplish the required action.
   (E)   The order may be enforced for up to two years from the day the notice
is given.
(Ord. 2000-3, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2001-6, passed 7-5-2001; Ord. 2006-5,
passed 10-5-2006; Ord. 2024-2, passed 3-7-2024) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 151.04 PERFORMANCE OF WORK AND COSTS THEREOF.
   The work required by an order of the Enforcement Authority may be performed
in the following manners.
   (A)   Work described in §
151.03 may be performed without further notice to the property owner and may be
performed by a contractor who has been awarded a base bid to perform the work,
or by the Enforcement Authority acting through its own works and equipment.
   (B)   All other work described in §
151.03, which is estimated to cost less than $5,000, may be performed after
notice to the property owner of at least ten days, by the Enforcement Authority
acting through its own employees and equipment. Work estimated to cost more
than $5,000, must be let at public bid to a contractor licensed and qualified
under law.
(Ord. 2000-3, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2006-5, passed 10-5-2006; Ord. 2024-2,
passed 3-7-2024)
§ 151.05 LIABILITY FOR COSTS.
   (A)   When action required by an order is performed by the Enforcement
Authority or by a contractor, each person, who held a substantial property
interest from the time the order was issued to the time the work was performed
is jointly and severally responsible for the costs thereof, pursuant to I.C.
36-7-9-12.
   (B)   Judgment for these costs shall be obtained pursuant to I.C. 36-7-9-13.
(Ord. 2000-3, passed 4-6-2000; Ord. 2006-5, passed 10-5-2006; Ord. 2024-2,
passed 3-7-2024)
CHAPTER 152: HOUSING CODE
Section
   
152.01   Definitions
   
152.02   Responsibilities of owners
   
152.03   Responsibilities of occupants
   
152.04   Building requirements
   
152.05   Unlawful disposal into sanitary system
   
152.06   Use of basement as dwelling unit
   
152.07   Notice of violations, contents, and service
   
152.08   Enforcement
 
   
152.99   Penalty
§ 152.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For purposes of this chapter, the words and phrases set out below that have
been specifically defined in this chapter shall have the meaning set out in
this chapter, unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 152.02 RESPONSIBILITIES OF OWNERS.
   (A)   Each owner of real estate within the town limits shall be responsible
for the following:
      (1)   Maintenance of every dwelling, building, or structure in a
condition that equals or exceeds the minimum standards set out in §
152.04;
      (2)   Maintenance in a clean and sanitary condition the shared or public
area of the dwelling and premises if there are more than four dwelling units in
the dwelling;
      (3)   Elimination of all fire and safety hazards, correction of
structural inadequacies, and maintenance of heating equipment and electrical
wiring in good repair;
      (4)   Removal of rotted wooden fences, rotted outbuildings, and frame
structures that may provide a harbor for mice and rats;
      (5)   Installation and maintenance of adequate water supplies in the
kitchen and bathroom areas;
      (6)   Maintenance of all sanitary fixtures in proper repair;
      (7)   Providing adequate drainage of premises;
      (8)   Elimination and prevention of rodent and vermin infestation;
      (9)   Provision of garbage disposal facilities or garbage containers for
all dwelling units in a dwelling containing more than four dwelling units, and
for all dwelling units located on premises where more than four dwelling units
share the same premises;
      (10)   Elimination of potential hazards on the land;
      (11)   Maintenance of the roof and spouting so the roof does not leak and
rainwater is drained and conveyed away from the building so there is no
significant dampness in the walls or ceilings; and
      (12)   No person, property owner, landlord, or property manager shall
knowingly agree to rent, lease, or allow a property to be occupied that is not
eligible for water service because of non-payment or under restriction due to
any town ordinance.
   (B)   (1)   Notwithstanding §
152.03, whenever infestation is caused by failure of the owner to maintain a
dwelling in a rat-proof or reasonable insect-proof condition, extermination
shall be the responsibility of the owner.
      (2)   Whenever infestation exists in two or more of the dwelling units in
any dwelling, or in the shared or public parts of any dwelling containing two
or more dwelling units, extermination thereof shall be the responsibility of
the owner.
   (C)   (1)   If an owner fails to satisfy the requirements of any portion of
this section, the Enforcement Officer shall send a written notice to the owner,
instructing the owner to correct the situation within 14 days; however, when in
the opinion of the Enforcement Officer such a nuisance constitutes an actual
menace and immediate threat to health, the Enforcement Officer shall give the
owner three days to correct the situation.
      (2)   Failure of the owner to comply with this notice shall be deemed a
violation and, upon conviction, the owner shall be subject to the penalty
provided in §
152.99.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.03 RESPONSIBILITIES OF OCCUPANTS.
   (A)   The occupants of any dwelling, building, or structure shall:
      (1)   Maintain in a clean and sanitary condition that part of the
dwelling, dwelling unit, and premises that he or she occupies and controls;
maintain active water service with the town at all times the dwelling is
occupied. Any occupied dwelling unit or residence without an active water
connection shall be deemed a safety hazard under §
153.04;
      (2)   Dispose of his or her rubbish in a clean and sanitary manner by
placing it in a trash container;
      (3)   Dispose of all garbage and any other organic waste that might
provide food for rodents in a clean and sanitary manner, by placing it in the
garbage disposal facilities or in the garbage storage containers;
      (4)   Exterminate any insects, rodents, or vermin found on the premises;
every occupant of a dwelling unit in a dwelling containing more than one
dwelling unit shall be responsible for such extermination whenever his or her
dwelling unit is the only one infested;
      (5)   Store all material so as to eliminate rodent infestation;
      (6)   Remove all accumulations of garbage, tin cans, paper, boxes,
appliances and/or furniture designed for indoor use, motor vehicle parts, scrap
metal, or any other waste material on a private lot or dwelling, as well as any
other material that causes an offensive odor;
      (7)   Remove all dismantled, partially dismantled, wrecked, junked or
non-operational, discarded vehicles, with the exception of those places legally
doing business as junk or salvage dealers; and
      (8)   Prevent an accumulation of rubbish on the porch, yard or general
premises of the property.
   (B)   (1)   If an occupant fails to satisfy the requirements of any portion
of division (A) above, the Enforcement Officer shall deliver a written notice
to the occupant, instructing the occupant to correct the situation in 14 days;
however, when in the opinion of the Enforcement Officer such nuisance
constitutes an actual menace and immediate threat to health, the Enforcement
Officer shall give the occupant no more than three days to correct the
situation.
      (2)   Failure of the occupant to comply with this notice shall be deemed
a violation and, upon conviction, the occupant shall be subject to the penalty
provided in § 152.09.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 152.04 BUILDING REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Safe and effective construction or installation. Every facility, piece
of equipment or utility required under this subchapter shall be so constructed
or installed that it will function safely and effectively, and shall be
maintained in satisfactory working condition so that it imposes no significant
risk to health or the integrity of the structure.
   (B)   Health or safety hazards. No building, vehicle, structure, receptacle,
yard, lot, premises, or part thereof, shall be constructed, made, used,
maintained, or operated in any manner that causes or produces any health or
safety hazards.
   (C)   Foundation or frame. Every foundation, floor, wall, ceiling, and roof
shall be reasonably weather-tight, watertight, and rodent-proof, and shall be
capable of affording privacy, and shall be kept in good repair.
   (D)   Exterior openings.
      (1)   Every window, exterior door, and basement hatchway shall be
reasonably weather-tight, watertight, and rodent-proof, and shall be kept in
sound working condition and good repair.
      (2)   Every door, aisle, passageway, or other means of exit shall be
arranged so as to provide a safe and adequate means of exit in case of fire or
other emergency.
   (E)   Stairs and porches. Every inside and outside stair, every porch and
every appurtenance thereto shall be so constructed as to be safe to use and
capable of supporting the load that normal use may cause to be placed thereon,
and shall be kept in sound condition and good repair.
   (F)   Plumbing fixtures. Every plumbing fixture and water waste pipe shall
be properly installed and maintained in good sanitary working condition, and
shall be free from significant leaks, as well as defects and obstructions that
significantly interfere with the free flow of water.
   (G)   Walls and roofs.
      (1)   Any portion of a building, appurtenance, or ornamentation on the
exterior thereof shall be of sufficient strength and stability, and shall be so
anchored, attached or fastened in place as to be capable of resisting a wind
pressure of one-half that specified for a new building of similar structure.
      (2)   No portion of any building shall be warped, buckled, or settled to
such an extent that walls or other structural portions have materially less
resistance to winds or earthquakes than is required of similar new
construction.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.05 UNLAWFUL DISPOSAL INTO SANITARY SYSTEM.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully or maliciously deposit any
material in any toilet, bathtub, sink, or other plumbing fixture that may
result in the obstruction of any sanitary sewer line. Liability on the part of
the occupant shall not relieve the owner of the responsibility of cleaning any
resultant blockage, but shall subject the occupant to the penalties of §
152.99 upon proper proof of such willful or malicious act.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.06 USE OF BASEMENT AS DWELLING UNIT.
   No basement of cellar shall be used as a dwelling unit unless:
   (A)   The floor and the walls are impervious to leakage of underground and
surface runoff water, and are insulated against dampness; and
   (B)   Every window, below the grade of the ground adjoining such window, has
a light well or area way extending at least 30 inches out from the window the
entire depth and width of the window.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.07 NOTICE OF VIOLATIONS, CONTENTS, AND SERVICE.
   (A)   Notice of violations. Whenever the Enforcement Officer determines that
there are reasonable grounds to believe that either an owner or occupant of
real estate has failed to assume the responsibilities imposed by §§
152.02 or
152.03, or an owner has failed to comply with the building requirements set out
in §
152.04, the Enforcement Officer shall give notice of such alleged violation as
required by this chapter within three days.
   (B)   Request for a hearing. Any person affected by any notice or order
issued pursuant to division (A) above, may request a hearing using the
procedure set out in this section.
   (C)   Notice served automatically becomes an order. Any notice served upon
an owner, occupant, or agent under this subchapter shall automatically become
an order of the Town Council, if the person does not present himself or herself
at the next regularly scheduled meeting of the Town Council.
   (D)   Appeal from a decision of the Town Council. Any person aggrieved by a
decision of the Town Council may seek relief by filing an action for relief in
the Circuit Court or Superior Court of the county within 30 days of the
decision of the Town Council.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.08 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   Subject to the appeal provisions of this subchapter, if an owner or
occupant fails to satisfy the obligation imposed in §§
152.02,
152.03, or
152.04, after having been ordered to do so, whether the order is actually
issued by the Town Council, or a notice of the Enforcement Officer
automatically becomes an order because no objection to that notice is made,
such person may be fined as set forth in § 152.09. Each day in which any
violations continues shall be deemed to be a separate offense.
   (B)   Nothing in this section shall be used to limit or change the liability
of an owner or occupant of a building for damages imposed upon him or her in
law or equity as a result of his or her willful or negligent conduct in the
maintenance of an unsafe building.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 152.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Failure to comply or to prove intent to comply will cause the order of
the Enforcement Officer or the Town Council to be sent to Superior Court for
judicial review.
   (B)   Whoever violates any provision of this chapter for which no penalty is
otherwise provided, shall be fined not more than $2,500. A separate offense
shall be deemed committed on each day that a violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 6-6-2024)
CHAPTER 153: RENTAL PROPERTIES
Section
   
153.01   Title
   
153.02   Definitions
   
153.03   Safe and habitable premises
   
153.04   Annual registration
   
153.05   Inspection
   
153.06   No third party beneficiaries
   
153.07   Conflict with other regulations
 
   
153.99   Penalty
Cross-reference:
   Discrimination in the sale or rental of housing, see §
94.04
§ 153.01 TITLE.
   This chapter shall be known as the “Rental Registration and Inspection
Program” of the town.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 153.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning. Words in
the singular shall include the plural, and words in the plural shall include
the singular.
   INSPECTION CERTIFICATE. A certificate issued by the Common Council of the
town which documents that a rental unit has passed inspection and the owner is
permitted to rent or lease the unit.
   INSPECTION OFFICERS. The following persons, working separately or together,
who shall enforce the provisions of this chapter:
      (1)   Fire Inspector, Fire Chief, or other designated officer;
      (2)   County Health Officer; and/or
      (3)   An officer designated by the Common Council.
   OCCUPANT. Any person, living, sleeping, cooking, or having physical or
actual possession of a rental unit.
   OWNER. One or more persons in whom is vested all or part of the legal title
to property. The term includes a mortgage or contract purchaser in possession.
   PERSON. An individual, a corporation, an association, a partnership, a
governmental entity, a trust, an estate, or any other legal or commercial
entity.
   REGISTRATION FEE. The amount paid to the Clerk-Treasurer of the town when
registering a rental unit with the town.
   RENTAL UNIT.
      (1)   A structure, or the part of a structure, that is used as a home,
residence, or sleeping unit by:
         (a)   One individual who maintains a household; or
         (b)   Two or more individuals who maintain a common household.
      (2)   Any grounds, facilities, or area promised for the use of a
residential tenant, including the following:
         (a)   An apartment unit;
         (b)   A boarding house;
         (c)   A rooming house;
         (d)   A mobile home space; and
         (e)   A single- or two- or more family dwelling.
   RENTAL UNIT COMMUNITY. One or more parcels of contiguous real property upon
which are located one or more structures containing rental units, if:
      (1)   The combined total of all rental units in all of the structures is
five or more rental units; and
      (2)   The rental units are not occupied solely by the owner or the
owner’s family.
   UNSAFE BUILDING. A building or structure, or any part of a building or
structure, that is:
      (1)   In an impaired structural condition that makes it unsafe to a
person or property;
      (2)   A fire hazard;
      (3)   A hazard to the public health;
      (4)   A public nuisance;
      (5)   Dangerous to a person or property because of a violation of a
statue or ordinance concerning building condition or maintenance;
      (6)   Vacant and not maintained in a manner that would allow human
habitation, occupancy, or use under the requirements of a statute or an
ordinance; or
      (7)   Otherwise in violation of state or town unsafe building laws.
   UNSAFE PREMISES. The tract of real estate on which an unsafe building is
located.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 153.03 SAFE AND HABITABLE PREMISES.
   An owner must maintain the rental unit in a safe and habitable manner.
Accordingly, the owner must ensure that a rental unit:
   (A)   Is not in an unsafe building;
   (B)   Is in compliance with all rules, regulations, ordinances, statutes, or
other laws including, but not limited to:
      (1)   The town’s unsafe building ordinance;
      (2)   The state’s Unsafe Building Law, being I.C. 36-7-9;
      (3)   The state and town Fire Code;
      (4)   The state and town Building Code;
      (5)   National, state, and local Electric Code; and
      (6)   Any other rule, regulation, statute, or other law relating or
pertaining to the safety or habitability of a residential or rental property.
   (C)   Is safe and habitable with respect to:
      (1)   Electrical supply and electrical systems;
      (2)   Plumbing and plumbing systems;
      (3)   Water supply, including hot water;
      (4)   Heating, ventilation, and air conditioning equipment and systems;
      (5)   Bathroom and toilet facilities;
      (6)   Doors, windows, stairways, and hallways;
      (7)   Functioning smoke detectors; and
      (8)   The structure in which a rental unit is located.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.04 ANNUAL REGISTRATION.
   (A)   Registration form.
      (1)   The Common Council shall prepare a form for an owner of a rental
unit to complete (“registration form”).
      (2)   The registration form shall require information including, but not
be limited to: name of owner, address of rental unit, mailing address for owner
or owner’s representative, name of tenant, e-mail address, phone number, number
of units that owner rents, and verification that the landlord will update any
and all information within 30 days of any change.
      (2)   The Common Council may amend the registration form from time to
time as appropriate and/or necessary.
   (B)   Registration and fee. An owner of rental unit in the town shall
complete a registration form and pay a $5 registration fee (“registration fee”)
for each parcel of real property on which a rental unit is located. The
registration form and the registration fee shall be submitted to the Town
Clerk-Treasurer’s office. The registration fee shall be paid once every five
years as long as the residence is operated as a rental unit.
   (C)   Rental unit community exception. Notwithstanding the provisions of
division (B) above, an owner of a rental unit community will only be obligated
to complete one registration form and to submit a single registration fee per
each rental unit community.
   (D)   Obligation to update information. The owner of a rental unit will be
required to update its registration form within 30 days of any change in
address, change in ownership, change in occupant, or any other material changes
thereto. Failure to do so will result in a violation of this chapter.
   (E)   Initial registration. All current owners shall submit an initial
registration form and a registration fee for any and all existing rental units
by September 1, 2024. Thereafter, any owner shall have 30 days from obtaining
ownership in a rental unit and/or leasing a rental unit to register that rental
unit with the town and to submit the registration fee.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 153.05 INSPECTION.
   (A)   Inspections authorized. The Inspection Officers are authorized and
directed to make inspections to determine the condition of rental units located
within the town. Possible reasons for inspections include, but are not limited
to: a change in the name of a water service account or the filing of a claim by
a tenant.
      (1)   (a)   The Inspection Officers are authorized to enter, examine, and
survey, at all reasonable times, any and all rental units.
         (b)   The owner or the owner’s representative, and/or occupant of
every rental unit shall give the Inspection Officer free access to such rental
unit and its premises at all reasonable times for the purpose of such
inspection, examination and survey; provided, however, that such Inspection
Officer has, prior to entry thereof, positively identified himself or herself
as a person authorized pursuant to this chapter to enter upon said premises.
         (c)   At the time of each inspection, all pets must be controlled so
that the Inspection Officer can move about the dwelling and surrounding
property.
      (2)   The owner or the owner’s representative and the occupant shall be
entitled to 72 hours’ written notice from the Inspection Officer prior to
conducting the inspection, examination or survey. In the event that the owner,
or the tenant if occupied, refuses to allow the Inspection Officer to conduct
the inspection, the Inspection Officer shall apply for a warrant to make the
inspection in accordance with I.C. 36-7-9-16.
      (3)   This provision shall not be construed to limit or restrain the
right of the Inspection Officer to make an inspection of any other building or
premises pursuant to any of the provisions of I.C. 36-7-9-1 et seq. or the
town’s ordinances concerning unsafe buildings or unsightly premises.
   (B)   Inspection at least once every five years. Every rental unit operated
and maintained in the town shall be inspected by the Common Council or their
designee upon the sale or transfer of ownership or change in water billing or
at least one time every five years (“routine inspection”). The routine
inspection shall be made to ascertain that the facility conforms to all
requirements of this chapter, any other ordinance of the town, and all statutes
of the state regarding such facilities.
   (C)   Exemption to routine inspection. Pursuant to I.C. 36-1-20-4.1(c),
except as provided in division (D) below, the town may not conduct a routine
inspection of a rental unit or impose a fee pertaining to the inspection of a
rental unit, if the rental unit satisfies all of the following:
      (1)   The rental unit is:
         (a)   Managed by a professional real estate manager; or
         (b)   Part of a rental unit community that is managed by a
professional real estate manager.
      (2)   During the previous 12 months, the rental unit has been inspected
or is part of a rental unit community that has been inspected by either of the
following:
         (a)   By or for:
            1.   The United States Department of Housing and Urban Development,
the State Housing and Community Development Authority, or another federal or
state agency; or
            2.   A financial institution or insurance company authorized to do
business in the state.
         (b)   By an inspector who:
            1.   Is a registered architect;
            2.   Is a professional engineer; or
            3.   Satisfies the qualifications of the Common Council such that
the inspector would qualify as an Inspection Officer.
         (c)   However, the inspector may not be an employee of the owner.
      (3)   A written inspection report of the inspection under division (C)(2)
above has been issued to the owner of the rental unit or rental unit community
(as applicable) that verifies that the rental unit or rental unit community is
safe and habitable with respect to:
         (a)   Electrical supply and electrical systems;
         (b)   Plumbing and plumbing systems;
         (c)   Water supply, including hot water;
         (d)   Heating, ventilation, and air conditioning equipment and
systems;
         (e)   Bathroom and toilet facilities;
         (f)   Doors, windows, stairways, and hallways;
         (g)   Functioning smoke detectors; and
         (h)   The structure in which a rental unit is located.
      (4)   The inspection report issued under division (C)(3) above is
delivered to the Common Council on or before the date of the scheduled
inspection.
   (D)   Additional inspections.
      (1)   In addition to the routine inspection, the town may inspect any
rental unit, if the political subdivision has reason to believe or receives a
complaint that the rental unit does not comply with applicable code
requirements, so long as the town provides 72 hours’ written notice as provided
in division (A)(2) above.
      (2)   There shall be no charge for the additional inspection.
   (E)   Access. Every occupant of a rental unit shall give the owner thereof
or the owner’s representative access to any part of such dwelling or rental
unit or its premises at all reasonable times for the purpose of making such
repairs or alterations as are necessary to effect compliance with the
provisions of this chapter.
   (F)   Inspection fee. There shall be no charge for any routine inspection or
additional inspection.
   (G)   Inspection certificate. The Common Council shall issue to the owner of
every registered and inspected rental unit an inspection certificate as proof
that the unit passed inspection. The inspection certificate shall be valid
until the next inspection.
   (H)   Violation notice. If an Inspection Officer finds that a rental unit or
any part thereof fails to comply with any standard set forth in this chapter,
any other ordinance of the town or any statute of the state, he or she shall
give notice of the alleged violation to the owner of the rental unit (the
“violation notice”). The violation notice shall be in writing and shall
reasonably describe the violation found. The violation notice shall further
specify the date by which the violation must be corrected.
   (I)   Service of violation notice. The violation notice shall be served upon
the owner or the owner’s representative, and the occupant of the rental unit.
The violation notice may be served by any of the following methods:
      (1)   Sending a copy of the violation notice by registered or certified
mail to the address of the owner and/or occupant as reflected on the
registration form;
      (2)   Delivering a copy of the violation notice personally to the person
to be notified;
      (3)   Leaving a copy of the violation notice at the address of the owner
and/or occupant as reflected on the registration form; and
      (4)   In the event that service cannot be obtained by foregoing methods,
the alternate means of service described in I.C. 36-7-9-25 may be used.
   (J)   Curing violations.
      (1)   A rental unit that the inspection officer finds to be unsafe or
uninhabitable shall be repaired so that it meets acceptable standards within 15
days of the violation notice. Any other violations shall be repaired within 30
days of the violation notice.
      (2)   Failure to cure a violation shall result in a violation of this
chapter and the owner may be cited into the Union City City Court or County
Superior Court. The Common Council may extend the period for cure for good
cause.
   (K)   Re-inspection. Upon termination of the applicable notice period as
provided in division (J) above, the town may re-inspect the property and charge
an inspection fee for any and all such re-inspections.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.06 NO THIRD PARTY BENEFICIARIES.
   This chapter does not and is not intended to confer any rights or remedies
upon any owner, occupant, or any other third party.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 153.07 CONFLICT WITH OTHER REGULATIONS.
   (A)   All ordinances and parts of ordinances inconsistent or in conflict
with the terms of this chapter are repealed to the extent of such inconsistency
or conflict.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter shall repeal or otherwise alter the town’s
Unsafe Building Code, or the town’s nuisance ordinances.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 153.99 PENALTY.
   Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall subject the violating
party to a fine not to exceed $500. Each day that a violation continues or
remains uncured shall constitute a separate offense of non-compliance of the
chapter.
(Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
CHAPTER 154: MOBILE HOMES
Section
   
154.01   Definition
   
154.02   Replacement of existing trailers
   
154.03   Parking
   
154.04   Exceptions
   
154.05   Trailer court
   
154.06   Hearings
   
154.07   Revocation
 
   
154.99   Penalty
§ 154.01 DEFINITION.
    A TRAILER shall be a vehicle without motive power, designed to be drawn by
a motor vehicle and to be used for human occupancy or for carrying persons and
property and which does not meet the structural requirements of a dwelling as
prescribed by the State Building Code.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970)
§ 154.02 REPLACEMENT OF EXISTING TRAILERS.
   Any owner may replace any existing trailer now parked on his or her land
only with a new or an improved used trailer; providing however, before
replacing the old trailer with a used trailer, said owner shall obtain written
permission from the Town Council.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.03 PARKING.
   (A)   A trailer shall not be parked within the limits of the town, except in
situations prescribed herein.
   (B)   A trailer shall not be temporarily or permanently occupied within the
limits of the town except in situations as prescribed herein.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.04 EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   A trailer may be parked in the rear yard of a lot and temporarily
occupied in case of illness of a relative of the resident family who may need
care and attention which he or she cannot otherwise receive. Prior to the
parking of a trailer, written permission shall be obtained from the Town
Council. The applicant shall furnish the Council with substantial evidence
confirming the health condition and relation of the person who is to occupy the
trailer and any other information required by the Council to satisfy the
request. After considering the request, and finding valid reasons for the same,
the Council may issue a 90-day permit. Such permit shall be renewable by
favorable action of the majority of the Town Council. A trailer permitted under
this section my be provided with electricity but shall not be connected to
sewer or water facilities and shall be removed with six days after the
expiration date of the permit.
   (B)   A trailer may be parked on a lot or parcel of land as temporary office
for a builder or contractor while construction is under way. Written permission
shall be obtained from the Council. The trailer shall be removed within six
days after completion or abandonment of the project.
   (C)   A trailer may be parked at any authorized trailer court in the town.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970)
§ 154.05 TRAILER COURT.
   (A)   A trailer court shall be an area or premises on which space available
for two or more trailers is rented, held out for rent, or on which free
occupancy for such number is permitted to trailer owners or users, not
including automobile, or trailer sales lots on which unoccupied trailers are
parked for purposes of inspection and sale.
   (B)   No trailer court shall be constructed, operated, or maintained in the
town without a permit from the Town Council. Applications for such permits
shall be made in writing and shall be accompanied by plans and specifications
sufficient to determine whether or not the applicant is able to comply with the
requirements contained in this chapter. The permit shall carry a fee of $100
minimum and $1 for each trailer space in the court, and shall be payable at the
time of filing for the application.
   (C)   (1)   All trailer courts shall have a minimum area of two acres.
      (2)   The minimum area to be occupied by one trailer shall be 2,500
square feet, clearly defined on the ground.
      (3)   All driveways within the court shall have a minimum width of 20
feet, shall be surfaced with durable, dust-proof, hard surface, and shall have
unobstructed access to a public street.
      (4)   Trailers shall not be closer than 20 feet to each other, nor closer
than 30 feet to any street right-of-way, nor within 25 feet of the boundaries
of the trailer court.
      (5)   Trailer courts shall comply with all local and state sanitary
regulations.
      (6)   Provisions shall be made for the handling and removal of garbage,
trash, and refuse.
      (7)   All entrances, exits, lanes, and driveways shall be lighted.
      (8)   No business shall be conducted in any trailer.
      (9)   Vehicles shall not be parked parallel with a trailer unless the
trailer lot is large enough to permit a ten-foot separation between vehicle and
trailer. Vehicles shall not be parked on drives, but shall be provided with
off-driveway parking.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.06 HEARINGS.
   Prior to the issuance of a permit for the construction and main tenance of a
trailer court, if any person or persons aggrieved by said issuance shall file a
written remonstrance, the Town Council shall within 15 days after said
remonstrance is filed, hold a public hearing to hear all interested persons as
to whether or not such a permit should be issued. The Council, after careful
consideration, will take whatever action is necessary.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970)
§ 154.07 REVOCATION.
   The Council may revoke any permit if, after investigation, it shall
determine that the standards of this chapter have been violated or that
irregularities exist in the maintenance of said trailer or trailer court.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970)
§ 154.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be fined
not less than $10 or more than $100 per offense. Each day that a violation is
permitted to exist shall or may constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 124, passed 4-7-1970)
